  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app',

  <span id="freeText4195738734568084491" style="display:none">Sarah O’Brien is alive because of the pact she and her brother made twelve years ago — James will protect her from their violent father if she promises to never leave him. For years, she’s watched James destroy his life to save hers. If all he asks for in return is her affection, she’ll give it freely.<br /><br />Until, with a tiny kiss and a broken mind, he asks for more than she can give.<br /><br />Sam Donavon has been James’ best friend — and the boy Sarah’s had a crush on — for as long as she can remember. As their forbidden relationship deepens, Sarah knows she’s in trouble. Quiet, serious Sam has decided he’s going to save her. Neither of them realizes James is far more unstable than her father ever was, or that he’s not about to let Sarah forget her half of the pact...</span>

<div id="review_287837346" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/287837346" />
    <a title="Tessamari ♥Many Waters...♥ ~ Sweet Spot Book Blog" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4597644-tessamari-many-waters-sweet-spot-book-blog"><img alt="Tessamari ♥Many Waters...♥ ~ Sweet Spot Book Blog" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1416791332p2/4597644.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/287837346?book_show_action=true">Mar 03, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tessamari ♥Many Waters...♥ ~ Sweet Spot Book Blog" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tessamari ♥Many Waters...♥ ~ Sweet Spot Book Blog" href="/user/show/4597644-tessamari-many-waters-sweet-spot-book-blog">Tessamari ♥Many Waters...♥ ~ Sweet Spot Book Blog</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/16167496-flawed">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4597644-tessamari-many-waters-sweet-spot-book-blog?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4597644-tessamari-many-waters-sweet-spot-book-blog?shelf=highly-emotional">highly-emotional</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4597644-tessamari-many-waters-sweet-spot-book-blog?shelf=crack-books">crack-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4597644-tessamari-many-waters-sweet-spot-book-blog?shelf=new-adult-mature-ya">new-adult-mature-ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4597644-tessamari-many-waters-sweet-spot-book-blog?shelf=must-re-read-again">must-re-read-again</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4597644-tessamari-many-waters-sweet-spot-book-blog?shelf=i-want-it-now">i-want-it-now</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4597644-tessamari-many-waters-sweet-spot-book-blog?shelf=november-2012">november-2012</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer287837346" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7174229180700616497">4.75-5 Stars<br/><br/><b>
  <u>**WARNING**</u>
</b> I’m an emotional wreck and cannot control the verbal vomit that will most likely come out of my mouth. So with that said, the following may contain spoilers and some expletives. You have been warned. Proceed at your own risk :) <br/><br/><i>You'll never know dear, how much I love you. Please don't take my sunshine away.</i><br/><br/><b>
  <i>“No, I love you. You’ve never loved me, even though it’s supposed to be me and you, forever.” He reaches for my waist and buries his sticky face in my stomach. “</i></b></span>
  <span id="freeText7174229180700616497" style="display:none">4.75-5 Stars<br><br><b>
  <u>**WARNING**</u>
</b> I’m an emotional wreck and cannot control the verbal vomit that will most likely come out of my mouth. So with that said, the following may contain spoilers and some expletives. You have been warned. Proceed at your own risk :) <br><br><i>You'll never know dear, how much I love you. Please don't take my sunshine away.</i><br><br><b>
  <i>“No, I love you. You’ve never loved me, even though it’s supposed to be me and you, forever.” He reaches for my waist and buries his sticky face in my stomach. “Why can’t I be enough? I want to be enough so fucking bad.” ~ James </i>
</b><br><br>Fuck. My. Life. I waited forever for this book to come out. The release date was pushed back so many times, I was ready to say <i>fuck it</i> and not even bother to read this. Alas, I had to find out if it was worth the wait. Well, let me state for the record: <b>This was worth the wait, well…at least to an extent.</b>This story is not fluffy and far from an easy read. This broke me. I’m hurt and I’m just flat out numb from the experience. I want to hate this, I really do, but I just can’t. It was definitely a <i>couldn’t put it down</i> story. Just be prepared for a <u>highly</u> emotional read. <br><br><b>
  <i>I have no idea what he sees in me. Strength, he says. Beauty. A big heart. I see none of these things. I see fear, flaws, and a heart so full of blackness I can’t give up my own selfish wants to set him or my brother free.</i>
</b><br><br>This story is told from our heroine, Sarah’s, POV. Her family life is fucked up. Her dad is an alcoholic and a former boxer with lots and lots of regrets. He takes out his drunken aggression out on his kids, James and Sarah. James has always been her protector; her savior. He takes the brunt of punches and does everything in his power to protect her. The only drawback to James’ protectiveness is his obsession with her. He makes her promise to never leave him. Their lives both revolve around each other. She cannot and will not do anything intentionally to hurt her beloved brother. The guilt he lays upon her binds her to him. However it becomes clear that his feelings for her is starting to become more than sisterly, especially when his best friend, Sam, is showing interest in her. <br><br>Sarah has been interested in Sam for as long as she can remember. When they start to form a relationship, her feelings are mixed with elation and worry. She can be herself with him. He knows her every flaw, both inside and outside ones. Even after seeing all her scars, he still loves her. She doesn’t understand why, but is grateful for the love and friendship he provides. Sam fills a big hole in Sarah’s life that James cannot fill, no matter how much he wants to. She doesn’t want to break her brother’s heart and knows James is capable of hurting Sam if he ever found out about them, so they keep hush-hush, at least for now. <br><br><b>
  <i>While being with Sam is every bit as incredible as I’d dreamt it’d be, he’s temporary. James is permanent.</i>
</b><br><br>While most stories are transparent and you know who the heroine should pick; most of the time, I want to smack some sense into her. However, this was not the case. I wanted her with Sam, more than anything, but I can understand her loyalty towards James. How could you not? He’s been her everything. After all they’ve been through, I understand her hesitance. Don’t get me wrong, I wanted her to choose Sam, but the choice really wasn’t easy to come by. My mind and heart hurt at Sarah’s predicament. <br><br>Towards the end of the book, my heart was racing and I was eager to know how this will all come to a close. Without spoiling much, let me just state that I was an emotional wreck, still am actually. I wanted to give the book less stars, but I just couldn’t. It was such a good story, but I wished the ending took a different route. <br><br>If you decide to read this, you are in for one heck of an emotional story. There are moments where you will cringe. I guarantee you will feel conflicted and your heart will be torn to shreds, but I cannot deny the long lasting impact this story had on me. So there you have it. Go forth and read this at your own risk. You will either hate it or appreciate it for the incredible emotions it’ll illicit from you.<br><br>----------<br>If you're interested, there is an alternate ending (which BTW, made me smile :)<br><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.kateavelynn.com/alternate-ending-2/">http://www.kateavelynn.com/alternate-...</a><br><br>----------<br>**Below is my rant regarding the drama surrounding the release date. I want to delete it, but decided I want to keep it for sentimental reasons. Teehee. ;)**<br><br>Update <s>July 31, 2012</s> September 10, 2012<br><br>What. The. F*ck!!?? Now <s>October</s> <b>November</b> release date? It was suppose to come out <s>tomorrow</s> October! What the f*ck is going on with this book? Just terrible. :-/<br><br>-----<br><b>

<div id="review_1196900505" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1196900505" />
    <a title="✦❋Arianna✦❋" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23370948-arianna"><img alt="✦❋Arianna✦❋" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1420671997p2/23370948.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1196900505?book_show_action=true">Feb 10, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="✦❋Arianna✦❋" class="user" itemprop="url" name="✦❋Arianna✦❋" href="/user/show/23370948-arianna">✦❋Arianna✦❋</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/16167496-flawed">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23370948-arianna?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23370948-arianna?shelf=dark-romance">dark-romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1196900505" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2903214795348552301"><b>4.5 STARS</b><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1423753865i/13667303.jpg' width='400' height='479' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“I’ll always love you and make you happy,<br/>If you only say the same.<br/>But if you leave me to love another,<br/>You’ll regret it all someday”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/><br/><br/>To say <i>“Flawed”</i> was an emotional read would be an understatement. I’m not gonna lie. I was exhausted when I finished this one. It was intense, heart breaking and depressing.<i>“Flawed”</i> is a story about life,family, love, loyalty, loss and so much more. It’s the story of Sarah and James, two brothers who grew up in a messed up home. Growing up with </span>
  <span id="freeText2903214795348552301" style="display:none"><b>4.5 STARS</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1423753865i/13667303.jpg" width="400" height="479" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“I’ll always love you and make you happy,<br>If you only say the same.<br>But if you leave me to love another,<br>You’ll regret it all someday”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br><br>To say <i>“Flawed”</i> was an emotional read would be an understatement. I’m not gonna lie. I was exhausted when I finished this one. It was intense, heart breaking and depressing.<i>“Flawed”</i> is a story about life,family, love, loyalty, loss and so much more. It’s the story of Sarah and James, two brothers who grew up in a messed up home. Growing up with an alcoholic, abusive father and a drug addict mother wasn’t easy for Sarah (17) and James (19). James has always been Sarah’s protector. He has always been her best friend and the only one who really loved and cared for her. Years ago he made her promise to never leave him, to always be with him and love him no matter what. They have to endure one more year in that house until Sarah finishes high school and then they will be free. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>”The only thing I want is to make you happy. You know that, right? Everything I do is because I love you”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br>If Sarah loves James like a brother, James wants more than a simple brother-sister relationship with her. Sarah had a crush on her brother’s friend Sam since forever, but he never was interested in her. At least she thought he wasn’t. But Sam secretly wanted and still wants more than a simple friendship with her. They start to spend some time together, they fall in love and they start a secret relationship to avoid problems with James. Everything changes for all of them when James finds out about Sarah and Sam’s relationship, that Sarah lied to him, that she betrayed him when he gave her everything. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“No, I love you. You’ve never loved me, even though it’s supposed to be me and you, forever.” He reaches for my waist and buries his sticky face in my stomach. “Why can’t I be enough? I want to be enough so fucking bad.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br>First and foremost I like to say how perfect the title is for this book. These characters are all flawed trying to find their way, to be free. What made this book interesting and different for me from other books with the same premise was James’s character. I could tell from the beginning that’s something about him, that he is different. <br><br>And obviously he is since he’s obsessed with his sister and so possessive with her. I like to think it’s not his fault that he turned out that way, even if he as so unstable and unpredictable. Maybe because I found his character so endearing. Years he sacrificed himself to protect his Sarah and to give her everything she needs. She’s the only one who matters to him. He is loving, caring and protective with her. But he’s also a lost boy. My heart broke for him. I like to think all he wanted and needed was love and affection. I really don’t know! For me he wasn’t an anti-hero at all. He was a likeable character, even if he has his flaws. James’s character development is very well done. I really, really felt for him and I also felt his love for Sarah and also his pain.<br><br>Sarah’s character was well developed as well. She is strong and determined to change her life and also her brother’s life and despite everything she still has hope. At times it was hard to be in her head and at times it was frustrating. I don’t know what I wanted her to do, but I wanted to try to save all of them. But of course she couldn’t. I liked her loyalty towards James and how powerful her connection with him is.<br><br>Sam was more a side-character to me. He was so great with Sarah. He is loving and tender and attentive. He is what Sarah needs, but maybe, just maybe not what Sarah wants, because at times she seemed to be in love with James as well. <br><br>The ending was devastating and emotional and I didn’t see it coming, but I was ok with it.<br><br>All in all, <i>“Flawed”</i> was a wonderful read with an intriguing forbidden theme, a captivating plot and complex characters.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"You are my sunshine, my only sunshine.<br>You make me happy when skies are grey. <br>You'll never know, dear, how much I love you.<br>Please don't take my sunshine away."</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="2903214795348552301" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_463185983" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/463185983" />
    <a title="Keertana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7584700-keertana"><img alt="Keertana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1438801223p2/7584700.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/463185983?book_show_action=true">Nov 25, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Keertana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Keertana" href="/user/show/7584700-keertana">Keertana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7584700-keertana?shelf=why-the-hype">why-the-hype</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer463185983" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4563473142035937307">Rating: 2.5 Stars<br/><br/>You need to know straight off the bat that this is one of those reviews you should take with a grain of salt. I read <i>Flawed</i> just after finishing Juliet Marillier’s masterpiece, <i>Daughter of the Forest,</i> and you should know, that reading order did no wonders for this novel. While both novels are vastly dissimilar, they both contain protagonists who have suffered through difficult situations and while Sorcha, the compelling heroine of Marillier’s tale, managed to make me weep and fe</span>
  <span id="freeText4563473142035937307" style="display:none">Rating: 2.5 Stars<br /><br />You need to know straight off the bat that this is one of those reviews you should take with a grain of salt. I read <i>Flawed</i> just after finishing Juliet Marillier’s masterpiece, <i>Daughter of the Forest,</i> and you should know, that reading order did no wonders for this novel. While both novels are vastly dissimilar, they both contain protagonists who have suffered through difficult situations and while Sorcha, the compelling heroine of Marillier’s tale, managed to make me weep and feel with intensity every feeling she felt, I unfortunately can’t say the same about Sarah, the protagonist of <i>Flawed. </i> Furthermore, <i>Flawed</i> is a novel that left me confused. I was forced to simply <i>think</i> about this book when I was finished with it – just not in a good way. It didn’t compel me to question society and think deeply about the issues this book covered, it simply made me think about why the book ended the way it did and how I actually felt about it – two questions I’m still not sure I entirely have the answers to. <br /><br /><i>Flawed</i> is one of the most perfectly names books I’ve come across. It <i>is</i> flawed, just as the characters and the lives they lead are as well. <i>Flawed</i> starts off immersing us into a world of horror, sadness, and misery. Sarah and her older brother, James, have grown up in an abusive household. Not only does their father repeatedly beat them, but their mother is a drug addict and as such, they have been forced to rely solely on one another as they’ve aged. At a young age itself, the two siblings made a pact: James would protect Sarah from their father’s beatings as long as Sarah promised never to leave him. While Sarah sees nothing harmful in this simple promise, the true repercussions of it are felt later on in her life as she begins to fall for Sam, the sweet-spoken and gentle friend of James. As James witnesses their romance blossoming, his own pent-up feelings for his sister – not-so brotherly ones, mind you – begin to come to the surface. In this flawed world, is there any real hope for Sarah? <br /><br />No, there isn’t. I hate to say it, but this book ends on a note that leaves me angry, upset, and feeling like I wasted my time because, to put it bluntly, this is <i>not</i> a story of hope. It isn’t even realistic, which is usually the other option when we are faced with novels that don’t feature around a theme of hopefulness. I’m getting ahead of myself though – we’ll talk about the end at the end. Firstly, what you need to know is that <i>Flawed</i> is a surprisingly quick read. It’s short, its chapters are short, and it will have you turning the pages in anticipation. Sarah and Sam’s romance is sweet – if you’re into sweet. I, on the other hand, yearned for more substance from Sam. If you liked Zeke from <i>The Immortal Rules</i> or Jase from <i>My Life Next Door, </i> then chances are you’ll love Sam. Like Zeke and Jase, Sam is perfect - <i>too</i> perfect. For a novel named <i>Flawed, </i> Sam ironically has none, which, for me, makes him a romantic interest who was sweet, but nothing else. <br /><br />Sam aside, Sarah was a compelling heroine. It was evident that she was torn, both between accepting her love for Sam and staying true to her promise to her brother. Sarah realizes that James’ feelings for her are not normal and while she keeps him at an arms length physically, she too realizes that she needs James just as much as he may need her. Unfortunately though, this is never further explored. We have on our hands an intriguing psychological situation of two siblings who are <i>too</i> close, all due to their circumstances, but we can never see the repercussions or true impact of this type of a relationship. It isn’t quite incest in the way <i>Forbidden</i> is – these two don’t love each other and they don’t struggle to want to be together. Instead, they rely on each other for support, but in an unhealthy manner. While I found this all very interesting, I was disappointed that this was never explored further. <br /><br />What prevented this novel from progressing to the depths it could have gone to? Well…the ending. It was convenient. Avelynn creates raw, tortured, and different characters, but instead of dealing with them, we have a rather convenient ending that very abruptly ends the story. A cop-out? I believe so. I guess readers were meant to cry and scream at the injustice of this ending or feel terrible for our protagonist, but contrary to all that, I just felt a massive dose of disappointment. Now, contemporary isn’t my preferred genre, so perhaps I go into it expecting a little bit more to really “wow” me, but somehow, this book failed to deliver. <br /><br />My personal qualms aside, as a piece of literature, I believe <i>Flawed</i> tackles on more than it can truly handle. We have an abusive father, a drug-addict mother, and two psychologically messed up siblings, one of whom is the victim of unrequited love with his own sister. Hmm…seems plenty complicated to me. Now, throw in a best friend romance, a protective older brother, lots of sneaking out to make-out, and some issues concerning sex and we literally have two books on our hands, only they’re smashed into one and the issues concerning both fail to be developed to their full potential or degree. <br /><br />All in all, I can’t say I really recommend <i>Flawed.</i> On the other hand, it was a novel that kept me entertained, captivated, and I enjoyed it a lot while reading it, but the overall impression it left with me was one of disappointment. I feel as if this novel could have been so much <i>more</i> and truly had the potential to resonate with the reader, but alas, I know this is one I’ll be forgetting easily. Yet, it seems as if I am – as I usually am, really – a black sheep when it comes to this novel. In fact, the majority of preliminary reviewers have loved this one and if you’re a fan of contemporary, issue books, or very sweet romances, you won’t be disappointed. If, however, contemporary isn’t your usual cup of tea, you only pick up issue books with severe persuasion, and you need your romances to have a little <i>more,</i> you may want to look elsewhere. <br /><br />You can read <a href="http://ivybookbindings.blogspot.com/2012/11/review-flawed-by-kate-avelynn.html" rel="nofollow noopener">this review</a> and more on my blog, <a href="http://ivybookbindings.blogspot.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Ivy Book Bindings.</a> </span>
  <a data-text-id="4563473142035937307" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10752235-l-a-i-n-e-y?shelf=na">na</a>,

  <span id="freeText5042745393499417747" style="display:none"><i>
  <blockquote>"Why can’t I be enough? <br>I want to be enough so fucking bad"</blockquote>
</i><br>Gosh. <br>This was messed up. <br><br>James O'Brien will <i>forever</i> be the character that I would have loved and shed real tears for <b>IF</b> I ever got the chance to get to know him. What a waste.<br><br>These people lives were so messed up and so so sad. It focused more on the troubles - the abusive father and the abandonment in their lives and not on the 'forbidden romance' aspect.<br><br>To be honest, I believe this book would be a whole lot more interesting if it was more about that pairing: James was such a compelling character, I really wish we could have seen him more. <br><br>This book dealt with a taboo subject and eventhough it has been compared to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1546098861" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Forbidden</a>, I have to say Flawed felt a lot more mature than that. That would the case of course since this book is NA while Forbidden is YA. Still the only real similarity between the two was the dissatisfaction I felt after turning the last pages. <br><br>I saw a lot of chemistry between James &amp; Sarah than her &amp; Sam.<br><br>[[note]] <b>I'm <i>soooo</i> not encouraging incest</b> but this is <b>FICTION</b>. <i>*whisper*</i> and I loved James!!<br><br><br>The central romance:<br><br><a href="https://media2.giphy.com/media/e4FV3I9fEvo76/giphy.gif" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1475635519ra/20744118.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b>Still</b> the book was emotional and intense. But the whole time I was reading and kept thinking "OK, you're good and all but could you please, just <i>pleaseee</i> give me James??"<br><br><br><br>Ps. oh my god, how many times did I say his name?!? Nuts!<br><br><br></span>

<div id="review_466614933" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/466614933" />
    <a title="Annie Brewer" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5315988-annie-brewer"><img alt="Annie Brewer" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442496062p2/5315988.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/466614933?book_show_action=true">Nov 29, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Annie Brewer" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Annie Brewer" href="/user/show/5315988-annie-brewer">Annie Brewer</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5315988-annie-brewer?shelf=new-adult">new-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5315988-annie-brewer?shelf=teen-sex">teen-sex</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5315988-annie-brewer?shelf=2013">2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5315988-annie-brewer?shelf=angst">angst</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5315988-annie-brewer?shelf=contemp-romance">contemp-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5315988-annie-brewer?shelf=favorite">favorite</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5315988-annie-brewer?shelf=tough-subject">tough-subject</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5315988-annie-brewer?shelf=emotionally-devastating">emotionally-devastating</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5315988-annie-brewer?shelf=death">death</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5315988-annie-brewer?shelf=total-mind-fuck">total-mind-fuck</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer466614933" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10195509532114510080">OH crap! I want to read this book...but ummm, after reading Forbidden and how it shattered my heart to the point of becoming inconsolable and not able to read another book for like a week, I am so scared to read this. Though these crazy, twisted, sick stories are always the ones that jump out at me and I always take the bait, I am just not sure if I can stomach this one. My heart is fragile as it is. Ugh, maybe I'll give it a chance at some point.<br/><br/>AHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHH</span>
  <span id="freeText10195509532114510080" style="display:none">OH crap! I want to read this book...but ummm, after reading Forbidden and how it shattered my heart to the point of becoming inconsolable and not able to read another book for like a week, I am so scared to read this. Though these crazy, twisted, sick stories are always the ones that jump out at me and I always take the bait, I am just not sure if I can stomach this one. My heart is fragile as it is. Ugh, maybe I'll give it a chance at some point.<br /><br />AHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHH<br /><br /><br />*SOB SOB SOB* What the fuck was that??????? OMG....O.M.F.G. I can't review this right now. I have to blow my nose ten times and sob on the bathroom floor for a little bit. <br /><br />~Review soon~<br /><br />This is going to be a hard review to write. I am still in shock and utter disbelief over this book...the ending. First of all, I want to commend the author for writing about such a taboo subject. I can't imagine how hard it was to write some of these scenes. I read Forbidden and vowed to never read a book like that again. I was tore up for days over that book and though this one is slightly different, it still had the same impact. Forbidden is actually one of my all-time favorite books ever and it happened to be the most devastating read for me as well. But this one was different. I loved it and some parts had me yelling and wanting to reach into my nook and strangle Sarah silly. But honestly, this was a very hard book to read.<br /><br />We have Sarah. She's about to be a senior in high school, she has one more year to be in the same house as...him. Her sick, asshole abusive father. She only has to endure one more year of his abuse and advances. But it's too much. Can she really survive one more year of his sickish fucked up tirades? *cringes*<br /><br />James, the savoir...the big brother who would do anything to protect his little sister from their father. Even if it meant locking her up so she can never see the outside world, except for him. When they were little, they made a pact that they would always be together...always stay together and live their lives, well together and she promised to never leave him. Except, both of their meanings differed. Where James wanted more from her than her love as a sister, things got complicated. She loves her brother, more than anyone...but not in the way James assumes. And though she would do anything for him since after all, he did throw himself in front of their father on more than one occasion to save her and for that he had bruises and scars to show the lengths he'd take to save her, it's a different kind of love. And in the end, it doesn't work in his favor.<br /><br />Sam Donavan...the amazing sweet guy whom I fell for instantly. He is, was I should say James' best friend since they were young. He was always by James's side. But also, he was in love with Sarah for years and never did anything about it...until now. But it might be too late. James has Sarah locked up like a prisoner. He wants to protect her from their father, but ends up wanting her for himself. He doesn't want her talking to his friends, go to college or get a job. He wants to do everything for her and in turn she has to do everything he wants. It's really sad. Sam tried to protect her and save her from all the shit she was forced to endure. But it broke my heart...he did his best. I wanted to punch Sarah on more than one occasion. She was stupid...really stupid. He offered her such an amazing future and he put his own future plans on hold for her. He had such a bright life ahead of him. *takes deep breaths* But he was so set on taking Sarah with him and then....*wipes stupid tears* and then, shit just gets real.<br /><br />This book pissed me off, moved me, made me swoon, made me cry, made me cringe, made me laugh, made me scream and last but not least, made me die inside. It was so powerful yet so devastating. I wasn't sure which way was up or down. I eventually understood why Sarah did some things but I was still upset with her. Her sick ass father finally got what he deserved, though I think he deserved far worse. Sam's mom was a saving grace in this. OMG, my heart....my fucking heart shattered into little pieces for that woman, yet it seemed to mend the slightest bit as well. James was so sick but my heart was also hurt for him too. It's not exactly his fault he turned out that way. And it just..it was...I just...*deep breaths, deep breaths Annie* I didn't hate him even though I wanted to. I wanted to hate him so bad....*breaths breaths breathe* But in the end, I just sobbed for him...them. All of them. What a clusterfuck of shit they all went through. Seriously.<br /><br />The end. I can't...but I...it just....Oh GAWD, *sob sob sob* Why??? Whyyyyyyyyy? Though this book was different than Forbidden, it was still the same numb, shocked feeling I felt. I eventually loved the characters and felt for all of them. I wished things had gone differently. I wished some things didn't happen. I wished some things did. I just wish. It's so hard to put into words what this book made me feel. How am I supposed to feel when I can't make sense of it all? Why did she? Why didn't she? Why why why.....that's all I can think. That's the word that comes to mind. But then again, being placed in her shoes,would I have done the same thing? I keep trying to figure that out. I guess in some weird crazy way, there is a happy ending of sort...but not the one we'd expect. Only thing I can say is thank God for Liz. <br /><br />Well done Kate. This book was hard to get into at first. I was very hesitant to read it but the writing was so real, it pulled me in pretty quick and I couldn't stop thinking about it when I wasn't reading it. So I guess that means something, right? I did enjoy it though, heartbreak and all.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10195509532114510080" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_510882209" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/510882209" />
    <a title="Rosalinda *KRASNORADA*" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12788865-rosalinda-krasnorada"><img alt="Rosalinda *KRASNORADA*" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1583582487p2/12788865.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/510882209?book_show_action=true">Jan 19, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rosalinda *KRASNORADA*" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rosalinda *KRASNORADA*" href="/user/show/12788865-rosalinda-krasnorada">Rosalinda *KRASNORADA*</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12788865-rosalinda-krasnorada?shelf=made-me-cry">made-me-cry</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12788865-rosalinda-krasnorada?shelf=amazing-writing-style">amazing-writing-style</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12788865-rosalinda-krasnorada?shelf=drama-drama-drama">drama-drama-drama</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer510882209" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13565456270317648189"><br/><br/><s>
  <b> I cannot rate this book but will try my best to review it</b>
</s><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380405827i/791118._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>I finally decided to rate this after 2 days, I cannot get this out of my head so I guess that's a good signal</b><br/><br/><s>Why can’t I rate the book? I don’t know, maybe I will be able to do it after a few days but most of the book I felt it was a 3 star book but then the end was a 5 star ending so it’s better if I just don’t rate it because my rating won’t be fair.</s><br/><br/>This is the story of James & Sarah. To be honest, I think this is their book, Sam wa</span>
  <span id="freeText13565456270317648189" style="display:none"><br><br><s>
  <b> I cannot rate this book but will try my best to review it</b>
</s><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380405827i/791118._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>I finally decided to rate this after 2 days, I cannot get this out of my head so I guess that's a good signal</b><br><br><s>Why can’t I rate the book? I don’t know, maybe I will be able to do it after a few days but most of the book I felt it was a 3 star book but then the end was a 5 star ending so it’s better if I just don’t rate it because my rating won’t be fair.</s><br><br>This is the story of James &amp; Sarah. To be honest, I think this is their book, Sam was one character but I didn’t feel him like one of the main characters. I knew, before starting the book the love between siblings was a one sided thing but Sarah confused me most of the time about her feelings for James.<br><br>James is sick, you can feel it from the beginning of the book. He was the main character for me, he was the one who needed help when all we did during his life was protecting other people. He is the one who made me cry, he is the one who will stay in my heart forever but just him, unfortunately I didn’t connect with the other characters as much as I connected with him.<br><br>He is a guy who is completely LOST. He’s been working to save money for his new life with Sarah, a new life they’ve been planning since forever. They live with their parents and specially their father is one of the worst characters I’ve read about in a book. How someone can be that bad of a person is beyond me. <br><br><b>It broke him, and in turn, he broke us all</b><br><br>But James is Sarah’s savior, as she calls him and he proves that every single time.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380405827i/791119.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Sarah and James are very close, not only in a brotherly way. James is obsessed with her (or in love, I don’t even know how to name it) and Sarah feels like she owes him everything, and she is kinda right.<br><br>She has a crush on James' best friend, Sam. Sam is a really nice guy who also happens to have feelings for Sarah (I never felt the spark between them but I was probably on James side as sick as that sounds).<br><br>They decide to start a secret relationship to avoid problems with James. Sam is obviously not happy hiding his feelings for Sarah but he doesn’t have too many options.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380405827ra/791120.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>***If you keep reading from this point you might read minor spoilers, pls be aware***</i><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380405827i/791121.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Their mother passes away and Sarah doesn’t feel anything. For her, her mother is the person that never helped her when she needed it but James it’s very affected.<br><br>As the time goes by, Sarah is falling for Sam badly. She meets Liz, Sam’s mother (my second favourite character) and she starts working with her on her flower shop. James doesn’t know any of this, obviously. Sam is still not happy with them hiding their relationship but he knows is best to keep everything secret.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380405827i/791122.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>James is not an idiot, he might be sick but he is smart and he suspects something is going on between Sam &amp; Sarah.<br><br><b>”The only thing I want is to make you happy. You know that, right?. Everything I do is because I love you”</b><br><br>And at this point I seriously had my doubts about Sarah’s feelings because she was apparently in love with Sam but some of her thoughts were confussing.<br><br><b>Sam’s quickly becoming my everything. He’ll never replace James, but Sam is exactly what my brother can never be</b><br><br>Of course he’ll never replace your brother and if you really see him as JUST your brother you would NOT compare your brother with your boyfriend unless you have more than brotherly feelings for him!<br>I understand she has had a very complicated life but I had that weird feeling during all the book, like she had feelings for him… never mind!<br><br><b>Nobody understands me better than my brother – they can’t, not without having lived the life we have. This is exactly why I love him and why, no matter how much I love Sam, I’m not sure I want to completely abandon my brother. Or whether I can.</b><br><br><b>I want to heal my brother, kiss his cuts and bruises and <u>lips</u>, and save him from what’s happening in my heart</b><br><br>I don’t really want to spoil the end of the book. I do want to mention I LOVED the author writing style and will read her next books. Will I read it knowing how I feel now? Hell yes, it was not an easy reading but I loved the end. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ HEA endings are NOT a must for me and the book could not end any better in my opinion  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br> <b>
  <i>I’ll always love you and make you happy,<br> If you only say the same.<br> But if you leave me to love another,<br> You’ll regret it all someday</i>
</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380405827i/791123._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>***UPDATE***<br><br><b>Mandy just sent me these alternate endings, pls read them, I loved both. <div id="review_286731803" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/286731803" />
    <a title="Katie(babs)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/179852-katie-babs"><img alt="Katie(babs)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1242522005p2/179852.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/286731803?book_show_action=true">Mar 01, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katie(babs)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katie(babs)" href="/user/show/179852-katie-babs">Katie(babs)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/179852-katie-babs?shelf=gag-worthy-book">gag-worthy-book</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer286731803" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2241293271717414383">It seems more young adult is tackling a lot more taboo subjects such as incest. We saw this with Tabitha Suzuma’s Forbidden, which is an incestuous romance between a brother and sister, both in high school. That book didn’t work for me for various reasons. When I heard about Flawed, and the possible incestuous implications that may occur about another brother and sister (but this time the sister isn’t interested at all), I would give it a shot. Flawed was a big disappointment, so much so that it</span>
  <span id="freeText2241293271717414383" style="display:none">It seems more young adult is tackling a lot more taboo subjects such as incest. We saw this with Tabitha Suzuma’s Forbidden, which is an incestuous romance between a brother and sister, both in high school. That book didn’t work for me for various reasons. When I heard about Flawed, and the possible incestuous implications that may occur about another brother and sister (but this time the sister isn’t interested at all), I would give it a shot. Flawed was a big disappointment, so much so that it’s the first book I ever sent back to Kindle for a refund.<br /><br />Flawed was horrid, and it's not because of the possible incest going on. Even the undertones of incest, mainly from James, the overprotective brother to Sarah was more ho-hum and tiresome after a while. The writing was disjointed and the over the top angst and abuse from the alcoholic dad (who lusts after the innocent, virginal Sarah) and druggie mom, who you blink and she’s gone, is so unrealistic. The flip flopping, wish-washy thoughts and feelings of the characters, mainly of James, and especially of Sarah- "I love James, oh no he's icky because he kissed me, but he protects me from incestuous drunk dad," was ridiculous and very grating. Sam, Sarah's knight and savior has some life in him, but he's a wasted character, more wallpaper than anything.<br /><br />If things had been more subtle with James’ and Sarah's home life and not the non-stop soap opera schlock within these pages, then this would have been so much better poignant and tragic tale the author was probably shooting for.<br /><br />This needed heavy content editing overall. There's really isn't much of a plot to speak of when it comes down to it. There's a mystery thrown in that makes no sense, and I can't tell you the number of times I rolled my eyes as I read who was responsible for the XYZ's clumsily laid out. The ending that's so shocking really isn't. It's a planned and blatant attempt to shock the reader into some sort of emotional response which fails.<br /><br />This is one DOA book. It's certainly not worth the $5.99. I've read better, well written and thought provoking self published young adult novels at half the price, and that's saying a lot.<br /><br />Big pass on this one.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2241293271717414383" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_481519441" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/481519441" />
    <a title="Debra" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13247178-debra"><img alt="Debra" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1473718933p2/13247178.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/481519441?book_show_action=true">Dec 20, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Debra" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Debra" href="/user/show/13247178-debra">Debra</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13247178-debra?shelf=tearjerkers">tearjerkers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13247178-debra?shelf=forbidden-love">forbidden-love</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer481519441" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16736627129357941121"><br/><i>"You are my sunshine, my only sunshine.<br/>You make me happy when skies are grey. <br/>You'll never know, dear, how much I love you.<br/>Please don't take my sunshine away."</i><br/><br/><p>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380401442ra/779209.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</p><br/><br/><b>
  <i>A girl desperately trying to escape her horrible life.<br/><br/>She's trying to escape her abusive father, her uncaring mother and her overprotective brother.<br/><br/>Then she falls in love with a boy...<br/><br/>A boy, who wants nothing more than to make her happy and keep her safe...<br/><br/>But, will her possessive brother and controlling father allow them to be toge</i></b></span>
  <span id="freeText16736627129357941121" style="display:none"><br><i>"You are my sunshine, my only sunshine.<br>You make me happy when skies are grey. <br>You'll never know, dear, how much I love you.<br>Please don't take my sunshine away."</i><br><br><p>
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380401442ra/779209.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</p><br><br><b>
  <i>A girl desperately trying to escape her horrible life.<br><br>She's trying to escape her abusive father, her uncaring mother and her overprotective brother.<br><br>Then she falls in love with a boy...<br><br>A boy, who wants nothing more than to make her happy and keep her safe...<br><br>But, will her possessive brother and controlling father allow them to be together?<br><br>Will she finally find her one true happiness in life?<br><br>Will she finally be free?</i>
</b><br><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380401442i/779210.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"I have no idea what he sees in me. Strength, he says. Beauty. A big heart. I see none of these things. I see fear, flaws and a heart so full of blackness I can't give up on my own selfish wants to set him or my brother free." ~ Sarah</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br>Before I started reading <i>Flawed</i>, I was warned that it would be a very emotional read and I have to agree, it definitely did bring out a lot of emotions while I was reading it. It always makes me sad and powerless whenever I read about children getting abused by their parents, and this book was no exception. I seriously hated Sarah and James' father, he was an ex-boxer taking the fact that he failed in life out on two vulnerable children and it made me sick reading about some of the things he did to them. Luckily, the scenes weren't too explicit though, so it was still bearable to get through...<br><br>The reason I'm giving this book a 3 instead of a 4 star rating is because I wasn't as wrapped up in the story as I expected to be. Somehow, I couldn't fully connect to the characters and their feelings. Maybe it was the writing style or the fact that it was written in first person tense, I'm not sure... All I can say is that the story didn't manage to completely grasp my attention. Maybe it would have been better if it would've been written in a dual POV... Nonetheless, I still enjoyed reading the book and especially the scenes between Sarah and Sam, the boy she's falling in love with. They were sweet and beautiful and I think those were the scenes that made this book for me...<br><br><br>~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~<br><br><i>"I"ll always love you and make you happy,<br>If you will only say the same.<br>But it you leave me to love another,<br>You'll regret it all someday."</i><br><br><br><b>WARNING:</b> The ending is unbelievably sad, heart wrenching and emotional. I did not see it coming and I honestly don't think it could have ended any worse...<p>
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380398015ra/768710.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</p><p>
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380401442ra/779211.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</p><br><br>This book might not be for everyone but still I'd recommend you to give this unique story a try and find out for yourselves... <br><br><br><b>3.5 heartbreakingly beautiful STARS</b><br><br><br>****<br><br><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="16736627129357941121" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_462078612" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/462078612" />
    <a title="Christy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11284813-christy"><img alt="Christy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1594293998p2/11284813.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/462078612?book_show_action=true">Nov 23, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christy" href="/user/show/11284813-christy">Christy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Anyone wanting an emotional, dark read and is okay with no HEA. </span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer462078612" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8932886720905870365">This was a story of devotion, loyalty, tragedy, love, guilt, beauty, and betrayal. At times I loved it, other times I hated it. I was angry, happy, disgusted, heartbroken and moved. After reading it I really felt emotionally raw.<br/><br/>After finishing this, I found myself thinking... <u>What did I just read???</u> It's been hours, and this book is still on my mind. I'm not sure how to rate or review this book... Overall, I'm still not exactly sure how I feel about it, but <b>I feel</b>.This book was not perfect, but</span>
  <span id="freeText8932886720905870365" style="display:none">This was a story of devotion, loyalty, tragedy, love, guilt, beauty, and betrayal. At times I loved it, other times I hated it. I was angry, happy, disgusted, heartbroken and moved. After reading it I really felt emotionally raw.<br /><br />After finishing this, I found myself thinking... <u>What did I just read???</u> It's been hours, and this book is still on my mind. I'm not sure how to rate or review this book... Overall, I'm still not exactly sure how I feel about it, but <b>I feel</b>.This book was not perfect, but when a story consumes my thoughts and makes me feel this way, I have to give it 5 stars. <br /><br />Sarah comes from a seriously messed up home life. Her mom is practically comatose, and her father is an abusive former boxer and alcoholic. The only person she can count on is James. James, her big brother is always there for her. He loves her and protects her. He can be a little obsessive at times, but they have a very close, dependent relationship.<br /><br /><b>
  <i> "I'm never gonna let anything happen to you, Sarah."<br /> "I won't let anything happen to you, too." He smiled, all dimples and sparkling blue eyes. <br />"Nah, you're too little. Just don't leave me, okay? Not ever. Promise."<br /> "I promise" <br />"You know why I do it right, why I let Dad do this to me instead of you? Because I love you."</i>
</b><br /><br />Sarah loves her brother, and he loves her. He has always made her feel safe. Towards the middle/end of the book, things start to change. You see just how complex James and her relationship is. James- he tugged at my heart. He was the main reason this book was so hard for me to read. He really did love his sister, but his feelings for her were not what they should be. James had some awful moments and made some terrible choices, but it was <u>so hard</u> for me to hate him. He was a victim too. Sarah and James father will always be the true monster of this story to me. <br /><br />James has two best friends: Sam and Alex. Sarah has had a crush on Sam for a while, and she finds out he has feelings for her as well. Sarah has never been allowed to date, and she is afraid of James to find out about their relationship. Sam and Sarah's relationship was beautiful. Finally someone loved her the right way. He was also a great friend to her. He made her feel safe, especially when things got complicated with James. Sam had his swoonworthy moments!<br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  <b>
    <i> "You think I don't know this went really fast? I didn't plan for this to happen. Hell, I didn't even know if you'd let me talk to you, much less be with you. But then you did, and we did, and... I figured out pretty quick that this is a forever thing for me. I think it has been from the very beginning.</i>
  </b>
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Sarah had some really difficult decisions to make. She was strong in a lot of ways, but she is torn between her love and loyalty.<br /><i>I've been hoping for a miracle that will let me keep Sam and James. Let me make them both happy. They deserve more than I can give them, but I'm too selfish, too loyal to let either go.</i><br /><br />The ending was devastating. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<i><b>"They are too late. They are always too late."</b></i>I can't believe Sam and James both had to die. Sarah had to loose the only two people who ever loved her. Not going to lie, I cried like a baby. I cried for Sarah. I cried for Sam. And I cried for James. It was messed up. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. If you are looking for a book with a HEA, this won't be a good fit for you. This book will leave you an emotional wreck. It was intense. It was compelling. Once I started it, I couldn't put it down. It's not an easy read, read at your own risk! </span>
  <a data-text-id="8932886720905870365" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/464115617?book_show_action=true">Nov 26, 2012</a>

<div id="review_479191026" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/479191026" />
    <a title="Aму" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10342872-a"><img alt="Aму" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1411959522p2/10342872.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/479191026?book_show_action=true">Dec 16, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aму" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aму" href="/user/show/10342872-a">Aму</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10342872-a?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10342872-a?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10342872-a?shelf=protective-brothers">protective-brothers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10342872-a?shelf=taboo-love">taboo-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10342872-a?shelf=highschool-romance">highschool-romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer479191026" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16163470622417243369"><b>**</b>Because of some of the comments that I've seen about this novel, I want to start by saying that this isn't a story about incest. That label feels misleading and many readers will be turned off when they're assuming that this features a romantic relationship between two siblings.<b>**</b><br/><br/>This is a really, really difficult review to write. Maybe that's fitting because Flawed was a difficult story to read. I think, by looking over the synopsis, the basics of the story are clear. Sarah O'Brien is the vic</span>
  <span id="freeText16163470622417243369" style="display:none"><b>**</b>Because of some of the comments that I've seen about this novel, I want to start by saying that this isn't a story about incest. That label feels misleading and many readers will be turned off when they're assuming that this features a romantic relationship between two siblings.<b>**</b><br /><br />This is a really, really difficult review to write. Maybe that's fitting because Flawed was a difficult story to read. I think, by looking over the synopsis, the basics of the story are clear. Sarah O'Brien is the victim of a horrific home life. Her brother James is her savior, taking her pain at one price, her love. All of her love. <br /><br />Though James certainly has his flaws, and he will make readers all kinds of unsure and uncomfortable, his determination to protect his sister is so endearing. He is a character I both love and hated, one that left me torn and twisted and ripped apart at times. Even if the story is told from Sarah's perspective, readers will connect just as strongly to James, and come to know him just as deeply. A victim of circumstance as much as his sister, and a boy who has given up so much in the name of protecting her, there is still something dark and dangerous about him. Heading down some rough paths of his own, James is as amazing as he is messed up. So he was naturally my favorite character. I loved the way the author made me second guess every motivation he had - caught myself many times thinking, "<i>Did he mean that as a brother.. or much much more</i><b>?</b> <i>Was nature or nurture responsible for his attitude</i><b>?</b>"<br /><br />Sarah is such an exceptionally well done character. A girl who has quite a road in this book, and who weathers it with both grace and mistakes. Her love and devotion for her brother is mirrored back in a way that is both hard to understand at first and not uncomfortable as much as bittersweet, but also something Avelynn does a tremendous job of explaining as things progress. Connected in ways they don't even seem to fully grasp, Sarah and James have a remarkably intense relationship that could not even be put aside at the signs of a broken mind. Maybe she never wants to believe James has a vulnerable side, but if things have been painful for her for over a decade living with a violent father, isn't it logical to assume that James could be suffering from some similar level of pain<b>?</b> (Her constant "<i>I love James, oh no he's icky because he kissed me, but he protects me from incestuous drunk dad</i>," was very grating at times.) But no, Sarah chooses not to think in a direction that would scare her even more. She never lets herself see how all the abuses have been corrupting James until it is too late. His sense of desperation pushes him to risk every bit of himself in his final attempt to ‘make things right’ and I felt totally exhausted and drowned in sadness as I finished the second last chapter of the book.<br /><br />Sam melts my heart. He is so caring, gentle, and kind. He is everything Sarah needs in life, even if she isn't at a point where she can recognize that yet. He has an understanding of what is happening with their father, but he quickly becomes suspicious of how possessive James is of Sarah. (I wonder if Sam had been feeling obnoxiously fed up with James for a very long time.) James was her rock through all the crappy moments in her life, so she had a hard time seeing the truth for what it was. I guess that was understandable, but it still frustrated me to no ends. I wanted her to open up to Sam when they finally got together or to anyone else for that matter, but she never did. The moments of peace, acceptance and love between Sam and Sarah were truly breath-taking. Even as much as she pushes him away at times, he still refuses to let her go. He knows it's not what she wants.<br /><br />Now, I also want to briefly talk about the ending. To say that I was perfectly satisfied with it would be the biggest lie ever. No. I was mad, frustrated, enraged and probably wanted to forget I even read the book. And then I thought about it really hard. I realized how much I actually appreciate the ending. It was realistic and consistent with Sarah's character. That is all I have to say. I'm not going to go further to ruin the reading experience for you, but be prepared to be absolutely angry at the ending.<br /><br />This one had a plot that was the perfect blend of internal, character focused portions, centered mostly on James and Sarah and more specifically all the realizations Sarah comes to, and external things that trigger quite the series of events. During one half of the book I was a sobbing mess and during the other half I was cringing at the cruelty that was Sarah's life. For a short read, it packed a lot of themes, real-life themes that some of us are most probably afraid to think of ; Incest,domestic violence,rape,teenage sex life,drug abuse. Personally, I thought Kate Avelynn handled them flawlessly (Get it<b>?</b> Muaha<b>!</b>). Her prose was simple, but extremely profound.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16163470622417243369" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer523835109" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer11604321177531218573"><a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[ She didn't die?!?!?! WTF! The only reason I kept reading was because I read a spoiler that everyone died...and then I find out that Sarah, AKA the Devil doesn't even die. <br/><br/>Not only doesn't she die, but everyone else dies and super speshul Sarah gets an HEA? WHERE IS THE JUSTICE?<br/><a href='http://s1299.photobucket.com/user/reblparn/media/tumblr_mdxihyofaW1qdn14l_zpseebe48a2.gif.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380407757ra/796827.gif' alt=' photo tumblr_mdxihyofaW1qdn14l_zpseebe48a2.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/></a><br/><br/>Okay, this book and I did not get along. At. All. <br/><br/>First, the protagonist. Super Speshul Sarah. She's not pretty folks, not a bit. Her eyes are too big for her head (um Disney Princess anyone?) and she's got</span></span>
  <span id="freeText11604321177531218573" style="display:none"><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ She didn't die?!?!?! WTF! The only reason I kept reading was because I read a spoiler that everyone died...and then I find out that Sarah, AKA the Devil doesn't even die. <br><br>Not only doesn't she die, but everyone else dies and super speshul Sarah gets an HEA? WHERE IS THE JUSTICE?<br><a href="http://s1299.photobucket.com/user/reblparn/media/tumblr_mdxihyofaW1qdn14l_zpseebe48a2.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380407757ra/796827.gif" alt=" photo tumblr_mdxihyofaW1qdn14l_zpseebe48a2.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a><br><br>Okay, this book and I did not get along. At. All. <br><br>First, the protagonist. Super Speshul Sarah. She's not pretty folks, not a bit. Her eyes are too big for her head (um Disney Princess anyone?) and she's got these horrible deformities called SCARS *eyeroll* and she doesn't think she's worthy of anyone's love because she can't do anything right and she has zero friends because her home life is soooo bad and everyone should just feel super sorry for her. <br><br>Nobody could ever love her, but her brother wants to have sex with her, as does her father, as does her brother's best friends. So pretty much every character in the book that's male (and that's pretty much every character in the book except for a placeholder motherly figure named Liz who's about as deep as a paperclip) wants to sleep with our MC. But SS Sarah can't begin to explain why all these people are so obsessed with her?<br><br> <a href="http://s1299.photobucket.com/user/reblparn/media/tumblr_mdulsfKyaM1rese01o1_500_zps73ae1cd2.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380407757ra/796828.gif" alt=" photo tumblr_mdulsfKyaM1rese01o1_500_zps73ae1cd2.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a><br> She's too innocent and sweet and naive to understand. <br><br>Good Grief. <br><br>So Sarah lives her life and we get to read about it, about how she cooks cheap boxed dinners and then there's a ten page scene of her at Super Cuts getting her haircut where James (her brother) stares at her creepily and while one hairstylist (slut) tries to get his attention the other one admits her jealousy to Sarah that she's got a boyfriend that is soooo obsessed with her. <br><br>LIKE AGAIN WTF?<br><br>Then they go to a party where she finds out her brother's been buying drugs, for the past six years but she's never noticed until this very night..umhmmm sure. <br><a href="http://s1299.photobucket.com/user/reblparn/media/Suspicious%20Skeptical/tumblr_me9gpkfDZi1rln1tdo1_400_zps41595397.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380407757ra/796829.gif" alt=" photo tumblr_me9gpkfDZi1rln1tdo1_400_zps41595397.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a><br><br>And also this very night this secret crush she's had on her brother's best friend comes to light and not only does Sam actually talk to her but he also explains his undying love for her and why he's always remained distant because James is super jealous. Because you know, James wants to bone her but she won't let him. <br><br>And also on this night she tells the reader that her brother has been showing up with bruises because he's been training/boxing at the Armory where all the locals go fight each other. <br><br>And then they go camping, so we get to read about how boring that is, but a bunch of *sluts* come and flirt with the guys but secretly everyone is too obsessed with Sarah to think much of them. And instead of swimming with everyone Sarah has to keep all her clothes on because of her scars and hide out in the tent and everyone feels bad for her, but really it makes her look classier than those *sluts* in their bikinis. <br><br>Then she hides the fact that she's seeing Sam from her brother, bones him, works for his Mom at the flower shop, and pines for Sam when he's not around. <br><br>Then she finds out James is fighting in the boxing matches and freaks out on him because he might get hurt (um...I thought he was fighting all along. That's why he was training wasn't it? I don't understand why she is an idiot).<br><br>Throughout all this her Dad has been hampering to get her alone so he can beat the shit out of her again, because that's his favorite thing to do, and while one minute James pretends to protect her the next he leaves her off in the woods somewhere and says she has to find her own way home. Because if he didn't then how would all the readers feel sorry for her all the time? <br><br>I'm telling you these characters were so one dimensional, so flat, so contradictory it was like they didn't really have personalities at all. They were just what the author wanted them to be when she needed them to be a certain way. Sarah's so timid yada yada, and then all the sudden Sarah yells at everyone. Bam, showed them. Ha! Yeah. Right. <br><br>So anyway, her Dad finally gets her alone and beats her and she goes to the hospital and Sam and James come face to face and know what's going on and James shoots Sam and then himself. But Sarah lives, to go to college and buy a house and plant a MOTHERF***** Rose garden. Like I said WTF? <br><br>I'm not saying James wasn't crazy, but good grief after living with her his entire life I can see how it could drive him there. Sarah hugged James, and cuddled James and kissed James on the cheek, and slept in his bed with him, spooning him, and changed clothes in front of him, and depended on him and pretended to be his wife and cook him dinner and I just think that their relationship was f****** weird.<br><br>I don't know...I don't even know what else to say. The only reason it's getting two stars is because it was barely decent enough to finish, even though I hated everyone, I still wanted to see the end. <br><br>And I realize I'm in the vast minority by hating this book but it was all just too soap opera dramatic and unrealistic and over the top for me to ever find any of it sad or deep or meaningful.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
