<div id="review_503875940" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/503875940" />
    <a title="K" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16359109-k"><img alt="K" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1357989852p2/16359109.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/503875940?book_show_action=true">Jan 12, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="K" class="user" itemprop="url" name="K" href="/user/show/16359109-k">K</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16359109-k?shelf=heart-wrenching">heart-wrenching</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16359109-k?shelf=made-me-cry">made-me-cry</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16359109-k?shelf=5-stars">5-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16359109-k?shelf=sweet-hero">sweet-hero</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16359109-k?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16359109-k?shelf=dark">dark</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16359109-k?shelf=forbidden">forbidden</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16359109-k?shelf=tragic">tragic</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer503875940" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16143405095637556611"><b>5 Breathtakingly-Haunting Stars</b><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380404778i/787996._SY540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"You are my sunshine, my only sunshine.<br/>You make me happy when skies are grey. <br/>You'll never know, dear, how much I love you.<br/>Please don't take my sunshine away."</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/><br/><b>Beautiful. Heart-Shattering. Devastating. Dark. Broken. Gut-Wrenching. Hope. Love. Forbidden. Taboo. </b><br/><br/>I loved this book so much! I was an emotional wreck after reading it. Don't compare it to Forbidden by Tabitha Suzuma, for while the taboo subject is there, it's completely different. This story is</span>
  <span id="freeText16143405095637556611" style="display:none"><b>5 Breathtakingly-Haunting Stars</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380404778i/787996._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"You are my sunshine, my only sunshine.<br>You make me happy when skies are grey. <br>You'll never know, dear, how much I love you.<br>Please don't take my sunshine away."</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br><b>Beautiful. Heart-Shattering. Devastating. Dark. Broken. Gut-Wrenching. Hope. Love. Forbidden. Taboo. </b><br><br>I loved this book so much! I was an emotional wreck after reading it. Don't compare it to Forbidden by Tabitha Suzuma, for while the taboo subject is there, it's completely different. This story is <i>not</i> for the faint of heart. This story has a lot of gruesome aspects. <b>This story is a tragedy, not a HEA. Have tissues handy, because I cried for a long time after reading this!</b><br><br><b>Sarah O'Brien the heroine was so strong!</b> Not in the physical sense, but in the sense that for all the years of abuse she has suffered, she has still remained hopeful. She's living a life that she doesn't deserve, stuck in an impossible situation, and trying to please the two people that she loves most. <b>Her brother James</b>, and the <b>man she's in love with Sam. <br><br></b> Her life is screwed up! Her father is a drunk ex boxer who takes his aggression out on his kids and wife. Her brother, James has always been her protector and savior. They were all the other had to lean on in the darkness. The only problem with that is from that darkness James falls in love with his sister. He becomes obsessed with her. Possessive. He wants her for himself, especially when his best friend Sam starts to show interest in Sarah. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380404778i/787997.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“This is my first real memory of James. In every memory before that, he’s just a flash of color, a warm body with a blurred face, a comforting voice begging me not to die. When he planted himself between our father and me that day, an eight-year-old with small fists clenched at his sides, I think I fell in love with my brother.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br>I <b>loved</b> James. <b>I ached for him entirely, he was so broken and I wanted to fix him.</b> He was unstable and unpredictable , but I couldn't help but see the goodness in him. He conflicted me. I hated him, then I loved him, then I hated him again. I loved him because he had good intentions. His whole life was devoted to protecting Sarah, and that love allowed darkness and madness consume him. <i>Tragic.</i><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i> “No, I love you. You’ve never loved me, even though it’s supposed to be me and you, forever.” He reaches for my waist and buries his sticky face in my stomach. “Why can’t I be enough? I want to be enough so fucking bad.” ~ James </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br><b>Sam, was amazing!</b> So romantic and loving to Sarah. I felt his love for Sarah, and I fell in love with him. Their love was forever.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380404778i/787998.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“You think I don’t know this went really fast? I didn’t plan for this to happen. Hell, I didn’t even know if you’d let me talk to you, much less be with you. But then you did and we did and…” He stops in the center of the room and stares at me, his shoulders sagging. “I figured out pretty quick that this is a forever thing for me. I think it has been from the very beginning.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote> <br><br>Once again, <i>Flawed is a dark themed book and should not be recommended to the faint hearted.</i><br>The writing itself is very raw with powerful emotions, it feels like your being slammed into a bullet train.<br>It's a thrill of a book, I couldn't put it down. Just be warned..<br><br><br><b>*****I would recommend this book to others*****</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="16143405095637556611" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Victoria Scott" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4658088-victoria-scott"><img alt="Victoria Scott" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1475325147p2/4658088.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/460639205?book_show_action=true">Nov 21, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Victoria Scott" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Victoria Scott" href="/user/show/4658088-victoria-scott">Victoria Scott</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer460639205" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7691116079501762186">Let me tell you something about how I read. Sometimes, I loll through a book, savoring every detail. Other times, I loll...but it's because I'm bored stiff. And on very RARE occasions, I turn into a raging lunatic who's prone to wild outbursts of irritation when anything--and I do mean ANYTHING--takes me away from the story in my hands. <br/><br/>Well, folks, Kate Avelynn's FLAWED had me lashing out like a banshee. Allow me to elaborate: <br/><br/>Husband: "Want something to eat?"<br/><br/>Me: *Snarls* *turns page*<br/><br/>Mother: "A</span>
  <span id="freeText7691116079501762186" style="display:none">Let me tell you something about how I read. Sometimes, I loll through a book, savoring every detail. Other times, I loll...but it's because I'm bored stiff. And on very RARE occasions, I turn into a raging lunatic who's prone to wild outbursts of irritation when anything--and I do mean ANYTHING--takes me away from the story in my hands. <br /><br />Well, folks, Kate Avelynn's FLAWED had me lashing out like a banshee. Allow me to elaborate: <br /><br />Husband: "Want something to eat?"<br /><br />Me: *Snarls* *turns page*<br /><br />Mother: "Are you driving down for Thanksgiving?" <br /><br />Me: *snarls* *turns page*<br /><br />Ghost of Abraham Lincoln: "I need you to perform a grave task. The fate of mankind depends on it." <br /><br />Me: "Back of, Abe. I'm effing reading."<br /><br /><br />Ah, FLAWED. I loved the characters. I loved the story. The ending broke me into a billion little pieces. <br /><br />I no longer feel like a real writer. <br /><br />Thank you, Kate. <br /><br />More, please. <br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_463814395" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/463814395" />
    <a title="Clarifina ~Books Are My Drugs~" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5854622-clarifina-books-are-my-drugs"><img alt="Clarifina ~Books Are My Drugs~" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1314684617p2/5854622.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/463814395?book_show_action=true">Nov 26, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Clarifina ~Books Are My Drugs~" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Clarifina ~Books Are My Drugs~" href="/user/show/5854622-clarifina-books-are-my-drugs">Clarifina ~Books Are My Drugs~</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Anyone who likes Forbidden or Love's Forbidden Flower.</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5854622-clarifina-books-are-my-drugs?shelf=books-i-love-like-chocolate">books-i-love-like-chocolate</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5854622-clarifina-books-are-my-drugs?shelf=bad-boy-or-rock-stars-or-nice-jerks">bad-boy-or-rock-stars-or-nice-jerks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5854622-clarifina-books-are-my-drugs?shelf=i-was-a-sobbing-mess">i-was-a-sobbing-mess</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5854622-clarifina-books-are-my-drugs?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5854622-clarifina-books-are-my-drugs?shelf=sweet-guys">sweet-guys</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5854622-clarifina-books-are-my-drugs?shelf=messed-with-my-emotions">messed-with-my-emotions</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5854622-clarifina-books-are-my-drugs?shelf=depressing-as-hell">depressing-as-hell</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5854622-clarifina-books-are-my-drugs?shelf=made-my-heart-hurt">made-my-heart-hurt</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5854622-clarifina-books-are-my-drugs?shelf=beautifully-written-books">beautifully-written-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5854622-clarifina-books-are-my-drugs?shelf=drama-drama-and-oh-look-more-drama">drama-drama-and-oh-look-more-drama</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer463814395" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7268299523927484762"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380398817i/771058.jpg' width='400' height='400' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>        <br/><br/>       What can I say really? That Flawed shattered my heart? That I love it despite this fact? What else is new? Okay, so for some of you who don't want to read this book because of the incest factor, please don't be turned off by this. It's not really an incest novel. It's not like <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7600924.Forbidden' title='Forbidden by Tabitha Suzuma' rel='nofollow noopener'>Forbidden</a>-although I do think that fans of the novel would enjoy this-because there was no real romance going on between the two of them. I mean, it was kind of like a one-sided thing...<br/><br/>       Anyway, Flawed</span>
  <span id="freeText7268299523927484762" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380398817i/771058.jpg" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg">        <br><br>       What can I say really? That Flawed shattered my heart? That I love it despite this fact? What else is new? Okay, so for some of you who don't want to read this book because of the incest factor, please don't be turned off by this. It's not really an incest novel. It's not like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7600924.Forbidden" title="Forbidden by Tabitha Suzuma" rel="nofollow noopener">Forbidden</a>-although I do think that fans of the novel would enjoy this-because there was no real romance going on between the two of them. I mean, it was kind of like a one-sided thing...<br><br>       Anyway, Flawed is about two siblings, Sarah and James O'Brien. They live in a home with their abusive father who was a former boxer and a mother who locks herself up in her room and probably couldn't care less about what happened to her children.<br><br><b>“Two babies in little more than a year and a half. Knockout Jimmy was forced to give up boxing and take a job in the paper mill.<br>It broke him, and in turn, he broke us all”</b><br><br>       Afraid to tell anyone about what goes on in their "perfect little home", James and Sarah depend only on each other. And so, they made a pact...<br><br><b>“I’m never gonna let anything happen to you, Sarah.”<br>“I won’t let anything happen to you, too.”<br>He smiled, all dimples and sparkling blue eyes. “Nah, you’re too little. Just don’t leave me, okay? Not ever. Promise?”<br>“I promise.”</b><br><br>...a pact which has a much darker meaning...<br><br><b>“And then James closes the last bit of distance between us and kisses me.”</b><br><br>...a pact that Sarah realises too late may be so much harder to keep than she anticipated...<br><br><b>“I feel his intense gaze skimming my face and force myself to look him in the eye. This time, when he leans closer, I know what he wants. He traces my jaw with his fingertips, then moves lower to my chin. My eyelids flutter closed when he tips my face up.”</b> <br><br>...especially when her life-long crush-Sam a.k.a James' best friend-takes an interest in her...<br><br>She starts to fall in love with him, trying to find happiness in the darkness called her life...<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380398817i/771059._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>James took countless beatings for her and all he asks in return is her unconditional love....but love is all Sarah has left to give. <br><br>Sometimes you have to let go of the people you love to move on but what if that person is the only reason you keep living for; for going on despite how much it hurts. What then? What do you do when the only reason you have to take in your next breath...is about to leave?<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380398817i/771060._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>...even if it hurts the person you love...<br><br><b>“Save James,” she whispers to me”</b><br><br>So this is where Sarah has to make a choice; keep the only person who was there for her when there was no light in her life or the person who brought the light to her when she was enveloped by the darkness...but the wrong choice could cost her everything...<br><br>But when she finally makes a decision...it may just be too late...for both of them...<br><br><b>“Save James, she had said, but I’m too late”</b><br><br>And so when all is said and done, she does the only thing she can do; she moves on...<br><br><b>"There's nowhere to go but forward, I remind myself"</b><br><br>...because time will go on and it may or may not heal all the wounds that the past had brought. But time clears the vision of grief. And she was able to go on no matter how hard it was because she was finally able to see the the past clearly as what it was: the past. Nothing more, nothing less. And all that's left of it are the memories. The painful ones and the happy ones. <br><br><b><br>“If I’ve learned anything in the last twelve months, it’s that I’m far stronger than I ever thought possible.”</b><br><br>~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~<br><br><br>That's all I can say really. If I say more I think I'm going to give away what happens-if I haven't done that already. This book is probably not for everyone, I won't lie about that so um, just be prepared. Cheers!<br></span>
  <a data-text-id="7268299523927484762" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_330853328" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/330853328" />
    <a title="Jasprit" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4841793-jasprit"><img alt="Jasprit" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1456315622p2/4841793.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/330853328?book_show_action=true">May 16, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jasprit" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jasprit" href="/user/show/4841793-jasprit">Jasprit</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4841793-jasprit?shelf=arc-galley">arc-galley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4841793-jasprit?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4841793-jasprit?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4841793-jasprit?shelf=out-2012">out-2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4841793-jasprit?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4841793-jasprit?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4841793-jasprit?shelf=read-in-2012">read-in-2012</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer330853328" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5121732899292729451">4.5 stars<br/><br/>After finishing Flawed I felt like an empty shell, numb and raw. Sometimes I enjoy books which leave you feeling crushed, like your heart has been taken and thoroughly stomped on. It takes a lot for me to be left so affected by a book and only a few this year have been able to leave me feeling so overwrought with emotions.<br/><br/>I’d heard endless things about Flawed before picking it up, yes I was worried about its taboo subject, and it’s dark and gritty vibe. I even had Kate stop by on the bl</span>
  <span id="freeText5121732899292729451" style="display:none">4.5 stars<br /><br />After finishing Flawed I felt like an empty shell, numb and raw. Sometimes I enjoy books which leave you feeling crushed, like your heart has been taken and thoroughly stomped on. It takes a lot for me to be left so affected by a book and only a few this year have been able to leave me feeling so overwrought with emotions.<br /><br />I’d heard endless things about Flawed before picking it up, yes I was worried about its taboo subject, and it’s dark and gritty vibe. I even had Kate stop by on the blog and share a playlist for the book, but there was this incredible invisible string tugging me towards it. Despite everything I’d heard and knowing this book would be going down a dark path I knew I had to read this book.<br /><br />James and Sarah have a really close relationship; they’ve been through so much crap through their life, so each is like a constant pillar of support for the other. They both know without one another they never would have made it this far. But their close sibling bond is often mistaken for something else. James does go overboard a bit sometimes in Sarah’s eye’s playing the over protective brother role a bit too much, he doesn’t really want anyone to get to know her, he tends to escort her really everywhere. It’s no wonder Sarah’s fully dependent on James, he’s her only real friend. Plus he knows about everything she’s been through so she doesn’t feel the need to hide away from him. But Sarah’s always secretly liked James best friend Sam, not that he’s ever paid her any attention, she can’t even get two minutes to talk with the guy with James around. But James reluctantly agrees to take Sarah to a party one night, and just her luck Sam’s there too. Before you know it Sarah’s realised her interpretation of Sam’s feelings were all wrong, that maybe there is a chance of her finally being with someone that loves her other than her brother. But she knows James isn’t going to be too happy about it, her only chance is to sneak around behind James back, she doesn’t like lying to James but she really has no other choice. It’s the only way she can keep the two men she loves most in the world close to her.<br /><br />If by reading the blurb to Flawed, you’re thinking of not picking it up because of its taboo sounding subject, please don’t do this. Because Flawed seriously provided so much more. It was a masterfully woven story combining several gritty aspects and producing a powerful heart wrenching read.<br /><br />The Bittersweet relationship between Sam and Sarah left me with a gaping hole in my heart, they were so perfect for each other without realising it, with everything Sarah had been through and with an overbearing brother who escorted her everywhere Sam was so sweet. Which guy decides to put his neck constantly on the line knowing his girlfriend’s brother would go ballistic if he saw them together? Which guy would sneak around at all hours just to spend even just a few minutes with his girlfriend? Act indifferent when James was around, and always want the best for Sarah? Sam seriously turned me into a pile of mush with his sweetness, his and Sarah’s scenes were chillingly beautiful. I was constantly at the edge of my seat, biting my nails down to the core, worried they would get caught by James.<br /><br />The day and a half I read this in I didn’t want to talk to anyone, I didn’t want to work, I didn’t want to eat or sleep, I just wanted to lock myself away with this beautiful bittersweet book. Despite me having early inklings about which way this book could go, Avelynn managed to grab my heart and smash it some more, never in my life have I wanted a book to end a certain way than I wanted it with Flawed.<br /><br />There have been some incredible debut authors this year, but everyone Avelynn is definitely one to watch. She shook me to the core with this book and a week after finishing it I’m still a trembling mess. Flawed in my mind is an unputdownable brilliant read, one that I will never forget.<br /><br />I hugely recommend checking out this <a href="http://thereadersden.blogspot.co.uk/2012/06/guest-post-kate-avelynn-author-of.html" rel="nofollow noopener">playlist</a> for Flawed made by Kate Avelynn, whilst reading this book; honestly the songs resonated with me.<br /><br />Thank you Entangled for this review copy.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5121732899292729451" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_463653321" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/463653321" />
    <a title="Laura Kaye" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3703867-laura-kaye"><img alt="Laura Kaye" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1412349602p2/3703867.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/463653321?book_show_action=true">Nov 25, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Laura Kaye" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Laura Kaye" href="/user/show/3703867-laura-kaye">Laura Kaye</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer463653321" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10031899859343378339">I just finished this book an hour ago (after reading it every spare moment I could over the past 24 hours), and I'm not sure I've fully processed my reaction, but I still feel like I need to release some of what Flawed has made me feel. So here we go...<br/><br/>One thing is for sure: you cannot read Flawed and not have a strong emotional reaction. For me, reading this book kept my stomach tangled in knots. From the first chapter, you know things cannot possibly end well, but exactly what that ending will</span>
  <span id="freeText10031899859343378339" style="display:none">I just finished this book an hour ago (after reading it every spare moment I could over the past 24 hours), and I'm not sure I've fully processed my reaction, but I still feel like I need to release some of what Flawed has made me feel. So here we go...<br /><br />One thing is for sure: you cannot read Flawed and not have a strong emotional reaction. For me, reading this book kept my stomach tangled in knots. From the first chapter, you know things cannot possibly end well, but exactly what that ending will be you don't know until you're tied absolutely inside out in anxiety for all of them to find a way through the incredible darkness of James and Sarah's lives. By the midpoint of the story, I had a pretty good idea (perhaps fear?) of what the ending would be, but it was no less powerful or painful for that anticipation. There are moments of light in this book (Oh, Sam, I will always love you), but they actually make the dark moments more painful because you fear the characters will never be able to hold onto them. The author is masterful at evoking emotion.<br /><br />The characters themselves are vividly portrayed. That doesn't mean you'll always like them, or agree with them, or not want to scream at them, but you will acutely understand the feelings and loyalties and rationales that motivate them. The impossible choices. The twisted loyalties and identities abuse creates. The many shades of love. I cared about Sarah, James, and Sam. Right now, I'm hurting for them.<br /><br />I thought the author's voice possessed a real sense of truth. And the writing style has the most amazing...I don't know...starkness to it that somehow also created depth in the smallest collections of words. I was truly hooked. <br /><br />Note: This is contemporary young adult fiction. Notice I didn't say romance. Romance guarantees certain things in a story. Contemporary fiction does not. Just know that going in.<br /><br />I found flawed compelling and heartbreaking, and I highly recommend it.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10031899859343378339" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer12453709438631681566"><b> <u>4.5 Devoted Stars!!! </u></b> <br/><br/>I feel like I was punched in the stomach. Then put in a choke hold. And I loved every moment.<br/><br/>I might come back with 5 Stars. I need to think. I need to become one with my feelings. I need to go to church, pray for my sinful thoughts. <br/><br/>Well, I'm still not sure how I feel, it's been hours. I will say, this story shocked the ever-loving shit out of me. If you are looking for a "real" taboo story then this one is it. Right out of a twisted lifetime movie. I don't even want to t</span>
  <span id="freeText12453709438631681566" style="display:none"><b> <u>4.5 Devoted Stars!!! </u></b> <br /><br />I feel like I was punched in the stomach. Then put in a choke hold. And I loved every moment.<br /><br />I might come back with 5 Stars. I need to think. I need to become one with my feelings. I need to go to church, pray for my sinful thoughts. <br /><br />Well, I'm still not sure how I feel, it's been hours. I will say, this story shocked the ever-loving shit out of me. If you are looking for a "real" taboo story then this one is it. Right out of a twisted lifetime movie. I don't even want to tell my thoughts because I feel like you need to experience this one on your own. Ok, how do I explain this without giving spoilers, and making you think I've fell off my rocker? <br /><br /><b> <i>You are my sunshine, my only sunshine. You make me happy when skies are gray. You’ll never know, dear, how much I love you. Please don’t take my sunshine away. James, the savior. That’s the image of my brother I clung to. Still cling to. </i> </b><br /><br />Sarah and James grew up in the house of horrors, abuse being the only stability in their life. They only have one another to lean on, to love. They make a pact to stay together forever. Sarah begins to wonder how much is too much when it comes to brotherly love. <br /><br />This book is definitely gonna grab you by the balls, and most likely you won't escape unscathed. I had these conflicting emotions through the entire book. Like, why would I think this is ok? This kind of love is not okay. But the author gives you this bond that's almost impossible to penetrate, and I really didn't want to. In which disturbed me to no end. The connection was beautiful in a disturbing, loving, I don't know how I feel way. <br /><br />Here's the deal. This book is for the risk takers, the people that don't mind if the characters don't get their white picket fence, for the readers of disturbing, for the ones that like jalapenos on their nachos. This story isn't black &amp; white, it's far from conventional, and it's not cupcakes and roses. So, with all that being said. I recommend to my sisters that love taboo and read the same books as I.<br /><br /><i> <b>"I’ll always love you and make you happy, If you will only say the same. But if you leave me to love another, You’ll regret it all someday." </b></i><br /><br />That was my warning. Now go read it!!!</span>

<div id="review_287489429" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/287489429" />
    <a title="Jessirae" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4487236-jessirae"><img alt="Jessirae" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1345364476p2/4487236.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/287489429?book_show_action=true">Mar 02, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessirae" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessirae" href="/user/show/4487236-jessirae">Jessirae</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4487236-jessirae?shelf=all-time-faves">all-time-faves</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4487236-jessirae?shelf=for-review">for-review</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer287489429" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10340906432081735335">Beautiful and devastating all wrapped in one heart shattering, soul moving book. Flawed broke me, crushed me whole and devoured my every being. Kate Avelynn created a book so powerful, so gut wrenching.. nothing will ever be the same. <br/><br/>Sarah O’Brien was the strongest protagonist I have ever encountered in all my time of reading. She wasn’t strong physically, but with years of abuse she had to go through, Sarah endured. She was living a life she didn’t deserve at all, stuck in an impossible situat</span>
  <span id="freeText10340906432081735335" style="display:none">Beautiful and devastating all wrapped in one heart shattering, soul moving book. Flawed broke me, crushed me whole and devoured my every being. Kate Avelynn created a book so powerful, so gut wrenching.. nothing will ever be the same. <br /><br />Sarah O’Brien was the strongest protagonist I have ever encountered in all my time of reading. She wasn’t strong physically, but with years of abuse she had to go through, Sarah endured. She was living a life she didn’t deserve at all, stuck in an impossible situation with difficult choices to make between the two people that she loved the most. It was all so hard on Sarah and I really felt that pain, the indecision and the stress she was holding on her shoulders. The juggling of protecting herself, her brother, and Sam just took a toll on Sarah and my heart damn near crumbled for her. In the toughest of times, Sarah held out and I truly looked up to the way she loved and cared for James and Sam. I loved Sarah for all that she was and all that she wasn’t and I especially loved her for the choices she made and the fact that she continued to dream, hope and live.  <br /><br />In so little words, I loved James. I ached for him entirely; that broken boy I wanted to fix from the inside out. As unstable and unpredictable as he was, I could not help but only see the goodness of his intentions and of his heart. He conflicted me, he shook me and made me love and hate him simultaneously. All his life has been devoted to protect and care for Sarah. Everything he had ever done was for Sarah and his unwavering love for her allowed darkness and madness to consume him. James only knew what he had to do to protect Sarah and all he wanted in return was love; love she could not give. And that possessive, all consuming love he had for her was what blew out the last of the bright flame my lovely golden boy had. How do you fix something so broken, so tainted by abuse, alcohol, drugs and fear that only darkness remained? There really is only one answer.. you can’t. <br /><br />The romance of this book rooted and attached itself to me. I have never felt so intensely for the love that bloomed between Sarah and Sam. It was electric and it was paradise and it was dangerous in so many aspects. For me, the risk was worth it all. Sam opened Sarah’s eyes. His smart, independent, caring, and protective personality awakened Sarah and taught her the true meaning of unconditional love. He gave her happiness and what little freedom she could take. Sarah was his everything, his forever and I truly believed that from the bottom of my heart. This boy.. this great, spectacular, unlike-no-one-in-this-world kind of boy was the sweetest, brightest and selfless being I have ever had the privilege to fall in love with. If there is one true hero in this book, it was Sam Donavan. No questions asked. <br /><br />I was unprepared for the amount of pain and hurt this book made me feel. I was unprepared for the amount and depth of love I had for every single letter, word, sentence, paragraph, page and chapter. I have never felt so much fear, hot and cold in my heart. I didn’t think I could have ever foreseen it coming at all. This book opened my eyes to the meaning of sacrifices, of choices, and complete devotion. <br /><br />Flawed has easily worked its way to being one of the best books I have ever read. The wait was more than worth it and if I had to wait a million years for this book, I would happily do so. Kate Avelynn completely moved me to sobbing tears with her clean, exquisite, and top notch writing. What she created in Flawed was pure emotion, passion and dark tragedy that shattered my heart to tiny painful pieces. It’s the type of book that is too beautiful for words and one that will haunt your very core to oblivion.  <br /><br />Overall, Flawed was just perfect, flawless and incomparable.<br /><br />More Reviews on my blog: <a href="http://jessiraelloyd.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Words, Pages, and Books</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="10340906432081735335" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_287359777" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/287359777" />
    <a title="Jena" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4021022-jena"><img alt="Jena" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1536102319p2/4021022.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/287359777?book_show_action=true">Mar 02, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jena" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jena" href="/user/show/4021022-jena">Jena</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4021022-jena?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4021022-jena?shelf=favorite-boys">favorite-boys</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4021022-jena?shelf=favorite-covers">favorite-covers</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer287359777" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6392037106570739302">This book hurts my heart. It hurts my soul. Shattered me into a million pieces. These words... Like razor blades across my skin. It's beautiful and intense and earth shattering. Flawed takes love and twists it into something deadly.<br/><br/>When you're put in an impossible choice, is there really a right answer? I have been there. Stuck between two heartbreaking decisions except there was no right choice. They are both right and they are both wrong... it always comes down to hurting yourself or the other</span>
  <span id="freeText6392037106570739302" style="display:none">This book hurts my heart. It hurts my soul. Shattered me into a million pieces. These words... Like razor blades across my skin. It's beautiful and intense and earth shattering. Flawed takes love and twists it into something deadly.<br /><br />When you're put in an impossible choice, is there really a right answer? I have been there. Stuck between two heartbreaking decisions except there was no right choice. They are both right and they are both wrong... it always comes down to hurting yourself or the other person. But with impossible choices, unfortunately I think you always lose regardless. You always hurt something with in yourself. Sarah sits in that spot. Shes so conflicted through out the whole book... family over love, love over family... love love love. She's been over protected her entire life, scarred, hurt, yet she still has love in her heart. I felt so deeply for her. And, I don't envy her.<br /><br />Then there is James. James is one of those characters that you either see the dark side or you see deeper inside and see that within that darkness is a boy who has been broken. Who's been strengthened to be overprotective. Who's had to turn himself into this twisted soul because he thought he was doing what he had to do for Sarah. James is the bad guy in this story, yet I somehow don't see him that way. He's good-looking, hard working, and protects the hell out of his sister. Some where along the line he just took it too far... too far to rein all that darkness back in. I still loved him and my heart still broke for him every time he shed a tear. Every time he was afraid to lose something too important to him. I mean, how do you just suddenly stop protecting the thing that means the most to you in the world? I know there is good in James. Unfortunately, he was just too far gone and I would have done anything to save him. He's that type of boy.<br /><br />Sam. He tore my world apart. Sam is Sarah's hero. I could never get enough of Sam. When Sam was filling the pages, my mind was completely attached. He's sweet. He's a family guy. He's smart. He's sexy as hell. He's protective. He's artistic. He's beautiful... inside and out. He has the type of love that could wrap you up in warmth from the inside out. He would do anything for Sarah... he does do anything for Sarah. "When are you going to get that you are everything?" (Pg 302). Sam was everything to me as the reader. I loved him so much, and his love completely captured my heart and then drug me down into that black hole of hurt with the bittersweet ending. "I figured out pretty quickly that this is a forever thing for me." (Pg 302)<br /><br />I could talk about this book forever. It will never leave me. I don't want it to. I want to look at that gorgeously haunting cover and know the story that lies within that broken weed.<br /><br />I devoured Flawed. I couldn't help it. I ate it's three hundred and some pages like it was fifty. It pulled me in piece by piece until it had all of me and then it blew me wide open shattering every piece of my carefully held in emotion. Yes, I cried. I held everything in. Each tension, each betrayal, each lie, each abuse, each torture, each kiss... Slowly building inside of me until that last chapter. When I found out that there was no going back, I couldn't hold it back anymore.<br /><br />Kate outdid herself with this story. It's heart-achingly beautiful and abusive. I fell in love with it and then it broke my heart. I've waited for this book for so long, it was my most anticipated book of this year and I can happily (with a broken heart) say that it did not disappoint me at all. It held up to every standard I put it to. It hit every bar I raised it to. I wanted some sick, twisted, intense book... and I got just that. I wanted to love a book that fit into that dark place in my soul... Flawed is that book.</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_634032277" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/634032277" />
    <a title="Katherine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13311251-katherine"><img alt="Katherine" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577842427p2/13311251.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/634032277?book_show_action=true">Jun 05, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katherine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katherine" href="/user/show/13311251-katherine">Katherine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13311251-katherine?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13311251-katherine?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13311251-katherine?shelf=dem-families-be-cray-cray">dem-families-be-cray-cray</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13311251-katherine?shelf=instalove-express">instalove-express</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13311251-katherine?shelf=siblings">siblings</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13311251-katherine?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13311251-katherine?shelf=coverly-love">coverly-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13311251-katherine?shelf=love-triangle">love-triangle</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer634032277" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7515179242821536357"><b>
  <i>”James is why I never left.<br/><br/>I should have left.”</i>
</b><br/><br/>I don’t know if this was intended of not (probably not), but the title of this book and it’s contents share are one on the same: flawed. <br/><br/>Sarah and James are siblings living in an extremely abusive household. With an alcoholic, abusive father and pill-addicted dishrag of a mother, there really isn’t much hope for these two kids. So when they’re children, they make a pact: James promises always to protect Sarah if she promises to never leave her. </span>
  <span id="freeText7515179242821536357" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>”James is why I never left.<br /><br />I should have left.”</i>
</b><br /><br />I don’t know if this was intended of not (probably not), but the title of this book and it’s contents share are one on the same: flawed. <br /><br />Sarah and James are siblings living in an extremely abusive household. With an alcoholic, abusive father and pill-addicted dishrag of a mother, there really isn’t much hope for these two kids. So when they’re children, they make a pact: James promises always to protect Sarah if she promises to never leave her. When you’re kids, promises take on a certain severity to them, so she agrees. Children who make promises also tend to forget them, so she fully expects him to forget their pact. What she doesn’t expect is that he in no way forgot, and he’ll do anything to keep her his, always. <br /><br />Man, do I feel conflicted over this one. And I think a lot of readers will too. Ironically, I don’t think it’ll be the subject matter that does it, but the choices the characters make and their actions (particularly the ending).<br /><br />What this book does show is the toxic nature of co-dependent relationships; everything form parent to child, brother to sister, romantic partner to romantic partner. The relationship between James and Sarah is a severely co-dependent. They’ve been abused to the point that all they have left to give hope to is each other. And yet, as another reviewer pointed out and I do have to agree with it, they need each other perhaps too much. A quote comes to mind from a romance movie I watched recently that I think perfectly describes their relationship: <blockquote>
  <i>’I don’t know where you end and I begin, and vice versa. You are the beginning and end of everything.</i>
</blockquote> When it comes to James and Sarah, they are so reliant on each other for everything that their brother and sister relationship is doing them more harm than good. <br /><br />One flaw (see what I did there?) that this novel did have was the relationship between Sarah and Sam. Sam is friends with James and has been the object of Sarah’s unrequited affection forever. They soon begin dating, much to the chagrin of James. I didn’t necessarily have a problem with the relationship itself, but I did question numerous times whether the relationship was just interested in their for their to be a catalyst. It went really fast (some relationships do, though), but I couldn’t help but feel that most of Sarah and Sam’s milestones as a couple were just written in there as convenient plot devices. That happens a lot in fiction, but it shouldn’t be obvious to the reader that it is. And Sam was just a little too… perfect. And I mean perfect. This was probably done to highlight the differences in him and James’ character, but it kind of made him vanilla in the process. <br /><br />Fair warning to readers, though: The reason James doesn’t like Sarah and Sam together is because of his unrequited romantic feelings he has for her. Yep, as if Sarah doesn’t have enough problems in her already fucked up life. I wish the novel could have gone deeper in the reason why and shown more sides to it. Readers might think of another YA incest novel when reading this, but unlike <i>Forbidden</i>, Sarah doesn’t return her brother’s feelings. Considering there isn’t a whole lot to go on in the ways of comparison, I would say the author did a commendable job.<br /><br />If this book could be described in a phrase, it would definitely have to be “Tell him the truth.” Because James hates the idea of Sarah being in a relationship with anyone, she and Sam have to keep their relationship a secret. The problem is that it’s the entire plot of the novel. With all the other serious issues going on in the book, you would think that there would be more plot than that. There isn’t though, and Sarah basically could have saved herself a whole lot of trouble if she did that. However, that plot felt more like the author only had that one plot in mind and had to keep stringing it out to create more substance for the reader. I’m not quite sure how I feel about that, but it did make the story drag out longer than I felt necessary. <br /><br />Again, I don’t know if it was intentional for the title and the contents to match, but it did. An average read with a potentially impactful message but it trips over itself with a plot that drags out forever and a too perfect love interest that only serves to be one character’s foil and nothing else.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7515179242821536357" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_288723992" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/288723992" />
    <a title="Amanda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3820088-amanda"><img alt="Amanda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1301523430p2/3820088.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/288723992?book_show_action=true">Mar 04, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amanda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amanda" href="/user/show/3820088-amanda">Amanda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer288723992" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10482645255926168610">Flawed has to be one of the best books I've read this year!! It was emotional, dark, intense book and full of love that it was overwhelming. From the very beginning I was hooked and that first page then went to 80 pages... it was addictive. Flawed was one of the best debuts I've read, and everyone who reads this book will fall in love with the chemistry between the characters and the intense plot. Kate Avelynn is officially one of my favorite authors because now this book will be stuck in my min</span>
  <span id="freeText10482645255926168610" style="display:none">Flawed has to be one of the best books I've read this year!! It was emotional, dark, intense book and full of love that it was overwhelming. From the very beginning I was hooked and that first page then went to 80 pages... it was addictive. Flawed was one of the best debuts I've read, and everyone who reads this book will fall in love with the chemistry between the characters and the intense plot. Kate Avelynn is officially one of my favorite authors because now this book will be stuck in my mind! I still havent started another book!<br /><br />When it begins we meet Sarah who is definitely a well put together characters, and is ready to move on from her broken family. She goes through this journey and self-discovery that it will blow you away. The close relationship with her brother is definitely uncomfortable at first because of their pact and the agreement that they would never leave each other. Avelynn did an amazing job of describing the relationship between Sarah and James because its an interesting relationship which is also sometimes hard to read without being emotional. Sarah faces a lot of hardships in the novel between her family and also the situations she is faced against. She was a great character and also relatable. <br /><br />James has to be one of the most complex characters when I was reading because he has a way of grabbing your attention but at the same time, was making certain scenes uncomfortable. He was Very protective of Sarah which was a love and hate relationship. He was to me a broken character with a lot of flaws but at times I just wanted to fix his problems. James is also a victim during the story which is another reason why the reader will feel his pain as well as Sarah's incredible story. <br /><br />Now to the amazing Sam Donovan *swoon* I think I fell in love with him the first time I read about him. Sam is definitely one man who will make you blush and fall in love because when Sam finally makes a move on Sarah (who has wanted his attention for years) the chemistry between these two makes me want to fall in love. He is another main character that plays a major role in Sarah's life and he was adorble, sweetm and his determination was dearing and made my heart race at times. Same is one of the sweetest boys you will read about, and watching his relationship develop was one of the best parts of reading the book because you see them starting to grow up together. His attention to Sarah makes the reader root for this couple to succeed. There were times that were emotional as well as bringing some tears to my eyes near the ending. But this beautiful book will make an impact on you. <br /><br />I was in tears involved but when I cry it means I loved the book, and see how connected I was to the characters and seeing the emotions that Sarah was going through. Flawed is definitely flawed but in a good amazing way because I can now say I am addicted to Avelynn writing now! From happiness, laughs and tears to OMG what happened, I did want more. With a great mix of sexiness and the raw emotions that will trigger many events in the book. This book is a MUST read because it is the total package and Flawed is a brillant read that is unputdownable!! </span>
  <a data-text-id="10482645255926168610" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1119697022?book_show_action=true">Nov 30, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Angela" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Angela" href="/user/show/30035966-angela">Angela</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1119697022" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15207675099656614723">I picked up <i>Flawed </i>because I'd never heard it brought up without <i>Forbidden </i>by Tabitha Suzuma being brought up after. <i>Forbidden </i>is one of my all time favorite books, so I knew I had to pick it up. I get why they are being constantly compared, but truth be told they have very little in common. If I would have read <i>Flawed </i>first I would have liked it more. That being said I still really enjoyed it.<br/><br/><div>
  <br/>
  <a href='http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-B8SMtlv7dCs/VLrwaXV-FMI/AAAAAAAABEc/UGaCIKb8PyI/s1600/flawed.gif' rel='nofollow noopener'>
    <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1421537585ra/13385792.gif' height='179' width='320' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
  </a>
</div><br/><br/>The back story between Sarah and James is dark and Kate leaves no detail unsaid. I loved</span>
  <span id="freeText15207675099656614723" style="display:none">I picked up <i>Flawed </i>because I'd never heard it brought up without <i>Forbidden </i>by Tabitha Suzuma being brought up after. <i>Forbidden </i>is one of my all time favorite books, so I knew I had to pick it up. I get why they are being constantly compared, but truth be told they have very little in common. If I would have read <i>Flawed </i>first I would have liked it more. That being said I still really enjoyed it.<br><br><div>
  <br>
  <a href="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-B8SMtlv7dCs/VLrwaXV-FMI/AAAAAAAABEc/UGaCIKb8PyI/s1600/flawed.gif" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1421537585ra/13385792.gif" height="179" width="320" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
</div><br><br>The back story between Sarah and James is dark and Kate leaves no detail unsaid. I loved how dark it got. <br><br>Her mom is practically comatose, and her father is an former boxer <br>turned abusive alcoholic. The only person she can count on is James.The relationship between them starts off so sweet. A bond that many would love to have with a sibling. But then their relationship turns too something wrong and sour. Sarah's character is weak and throughout the story is trying to find legs to stand one. She's trying to figure out who she is. James character goes from a strong leading male to a weak breaking human. Seeing the two switch places made for an interesting read. Then there's Sam. WHOOSH swoon worthy Sam. The moment he is introduced was the moment I fell for him. Each character too me had so many thing to like about them and thing about them I disliked. But all were so well written. Sam was without a doubt my favorite thing about this book. I couldn't get enough of him.<br><br><i>"I have no idea what he sees in me. Strength, he says. Beauty. A big <br>heart. I see none of these things. I see fear, flaws and a heart so full<br> of blackness I can't give up on my own selfish wants to set him or my <br>brother free." </i><br><br>The pace of this book is steady through out the whole book, and doesn't pick up much speed until the last handful of chapters. The ending more than made up for anything the plot lacked through out. It was the main reason I loved this book so much. Everything went down in the most perfectly heart pounding and heart punching ending ever. If this stories first half would have been as strong as the last half I would have given this book a higher rating. I even feel having it in dual POVs might have given it a little more edge. Either way it will be a book I recommend to many in the future. If you're looking for something a little on the darker emotional side <i>Flawed </i>is a good fit. <br><br><b><i>Flawed </i>is heavily weighed on one thing and one thing only... When stuck between a rock and a hard place, what choice would you make?<br><br><br>Read this review and more on our blog: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://southernbredsouthernread.blogspot.com/">http://southernbredsouthernread.blogs...</a><br><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://southernbredsouthernread.blogspot.com/">http://southernbredsouthernread.blogs...</a><br><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://southernbredsouthernread.blogspot.com/">http://southernbredsouthernread.blogs...</a></b></span>

    <a title="Sanny" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12051876-sanny"><img alt="Sanny" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1435527580p2/12051876.jpg" /></a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

<span id="freeTextContainer17660331327453715744">I can't rate this right now as my emotions are all over the place.<br/><br/><b>You told me once, dear, you really loved me<br/><br/>And no one else could come between.<br/><br/>But now you’ve left me and love another;<br/><br/>You have shattered all my dreams."</b><br/><br/>...neither am I sure where to start on my review, so first things first: this isn't a book I'd recommend - not because it was bad but because it talks about topics that not everyone can deal with.<br/><br/>The first sentence will hook you immediately. After reading that first sentence my min</span>
  <span id="freeText17660331327453715744" style="display:none">I can't rate this right now as my emotions are all over the place.<br /><br /><b>You told me once, dear, you really loved me<br /><br />And no one else could come between.<br /><br />But now you’ve left me and love another;<br /><br />You have shattered all my dreams."</b><br /><br />...neither am I sure where to start on my review, so first things first: this isn't a book I'd recommend - not because it was bad but because it talks about topics that not everyone can deal with.<br /><br />The first sentence will hook you immediately. After reading that first sentence my mind immediately started working out several ways for this story to play out. I was very tense throughout the whole book, waiting for the worst of the worst to happen - At this point I won't tell you if the worst of the worst happened, you'll have to find out yourself (or read another review :P).<br /><br />I always question myself why I read this kind of books and then this happens:<br /><br />some chapters had me literally holding my breath as my eyes flew over the pages to read faster, <br /><br />some chapters put me into a murderous rage, <br /><br />some chapters put a small smile on my face, <br /><br />some chapters made me cry, <br /><br />some chapters filled me with such a sense of dread that I haven't experienced in a book very often, <br /><br />some chapters overwhelmed me with compassion and pity,<br /><br />some chapters and the opening quote of this review broke me,<br /><br />but then there's the last chapter and sadness mixed with melanchony, as well as a strange sort of pride and hope.<br /><br />And then I know again why I read this, because the emotions are so close to the surface and always on the brink of overflowing, you have no other choice but to feel, no matter what it is that you feel.<br /><br />I was so mad for their lullaby that dragged throughout the whole book, but in the end I can't be mad because it prepared me for what was to happen even if I didn't want to acknowledge it (That probably sounds cryptic to you now, but I promise you'll understand in the second last chapter at latest). Just thinking about it brings another round of tears.<br /><br />On one hand, I wish that I could've read some chapters in James's POV but on the other hand, I think that reading in his POV would've utterly destroyed me, so I can't really decide if it's a small blessing or not that I didn't get to see the story through his eyes.<br /><br />Finishing my review, I've come to the conclusion that this book deserves 5 stars alone for evoking all of the emotions listed above. People will hate this book, people will love it, people will be disgusted but they WILL feel and that always deserves a full star review in my eyes.<br /><br />P.S.: I won't elaborate on all the things morally wrong with some characters in this book but I will say that no child should <b>ever</b> have think some of the thoughts mentioned in this book and my heart broke into pieces, knowing that some children think these thoughts.<br /></span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/365938695" />
    <a title="Anatea Oroz" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4183325-anatea-oroz"><img alt="Anatea Oroz" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1545147569p2/4183325.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/365938695?book_show_action=true">Jul 11, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anatea Oroz" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anatea Oroz" href="/user/show/4183325-anatea-oroz">Anatea Oroz</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer365938695" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1871609646249736048"><b>
  <a href='http://anateasbookshelf.blogspot.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>This review is also posted on my blog, Anatea's Bookshelf.</a>
</b><br/><br/><i>Amazing, Beautiful, Hart wrenching, Dark, Emotional, Powerful, Intense, Shattering, Overwhelming.</i><br/>These are just some of the emotions I experienced while reading this book. But they don't give the book justice, because what I felt while reading this book can not be expressed in words. <br/><br/>From the very beginning, I was sucked into the story and couldn't put the book down. When I finished it, I lay in my bed, unable to sleep and just thinki</span>
  <span id="freeText1871609646249736048" style="display:none"><b>
  <a href="http://anateasbookshelf.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">This review is also posted on my blog, Anatea's Bookshelf.</a>
</b><br /><br /><i>Amazing, Beautiful, Hart wrenching, Dark, Emotional, Powerful, Intense, Shattering, Overwhelming.</i><br />These are just some of the emotions I experienced while reading this book. But they don't give the book justice, because what I felt while reading this book can not be expressed in words. <br /><br />From the very beginning, I was sucked into the story and couldn't put the book down. When I finished it, I lay in my bed, unable to sleep and just thinking about the book. <br /><br />Sarah O'Brien was an amazingly strong protagonist. I felt so deep for her. For as long as she could remember she was abused by her father. Her mother was a drug addict and never there for her. The only person in her life who always looked out for her was her brother James. He promised her that he'll always be there for her and protect her, and in return, she promised to never leave him. She was living a life she didn't deserve. She was torn between leaving her brother and the guy she loved. There were so many things on her shoulders, so many decisions, hiding, lying and protecting herself, but still, she was strong and accepted everything as it was.<br /><br />James, Sarah's brother, also had it hard. Abused by his father, taking care of Sarah, it all lead to his instability. He loved Sarah, that much everyone could tell, but with time, his feelings for Sarah became something that was not normal, and that ruined their relationship. If it wasn't for James' protectivity and his wrong feelings, I think he could have been the best brother ever. I felt so sorry for James, he was a good person but some things from his past ruined his future.<br /><br />Sam was like an angel to all of them. He was a good friend to James, but the most important thing is that he was there for Sarah when life was the hardest for her. He cared, he looked out for her even tough he didn't have to. He was dragged into the mess just because he cared and because he was a good boyfriend.<br /><br />The ending was really hard for me. I don't think it is possible not to shed a tear at the ending. This is probably one of the best books I have ever read and I will remember it for quite some time. While this is not a book you can read whenever you want, you have to be emotionally prepared for what is coming, but it sure is a book you don't want to miss.<br /><br /><b><a href="http://anateasbookshelf.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/anateabookshelf" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/AnateasBookshelf?ref=hl" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://instagram.com/anateasbookshelf/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.pinterest.com/anatea92/" rel="nofollow noopener">Pinterest</a></b></span>
  <a data-text-id="1871609646249736048" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer2804635645256001186">⭐️⭐️<br/><br/>Not for me. Well written, but the ending just ruined it. I didn’t particularly cheer for neither Sam nor James, but you could say that I was leaning more into James. I know, I know, he’s her brother, but James’ character had so much depth more than Sam. Sam was just like a sideline character for me. He didn’t mean much at all.<br/><br/>Sarah and James, though, were from the same background to the T.   <span id="freeText2804635645256001186" style="display:none">⭐️⭐️<br /><br />Not for me. Well written, but the ending just ruined it. I didn’t particularly cheer for neither Sam nor James, but you could say that I was leaning more into James. I know, I know, he’s her brother, but James’ character had so much depth more than Sam. Sam was just like a sideline character for me. He didn’t mean much at all.<br /><br />Sarah and James, though, were from the same background to the T. They had the same pain and I think it resonated on how they would be in love with each other. Funny that she kept saying that she loved Sam and was disgusted about how obsessed James was about her, but I think she didn’t even realize herself that she WAS in love with James. She was more open to admit that she was in love with Sam because it wouldn’t be as wrong as admitting she was in love with James.<br /><br />But, still, siblings being in love because of their abusive upbringing is tragic. I genuinely think if Sarah were to give James a chance, he wouldn’t be so crazy. He just wanted to be enough for her.<br /><br />Anyway, because of the ending, man, it’s gotta be 3/10 worth the read. Felt like I was wasting my time reading this because of it. But, then again, I would be saying the same thing if she were to end up with Sam because he is SO boring. Whatever.</span>
