<div id="review_2990305729" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2990305729" />
    <a title="Anonymous Girl" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8605966-anonymous-girl"><img alt="Anonymous Girl" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1606187120p2/8605966.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2990305729?book_show_action=true">Oct 30, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anonymous Girl" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anonymous Girl" href="/user/show/8605966-anonymous-girl">Anonymous Girl</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2990305729" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11221515897014080289"><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1572489709ra/28378985.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><b>ABUSIVE THROUGHOUT...STAND-ALONE...3 DIFFERENT ENDINGS</b><br/><br/><b>
  <u>First Person Narrator: Sarah</u>
</b><br/>The story right from the beginning starts with the ending. From there I was already aware that this would be an emotional book. I am glum right now because despite not liking the story, I connected with the characters. I also appreciate the author for her additional endings which has lifted my 1-star rating to a 2 making it slightly <i>OKAY</i>. <br/><br/>The father is a boxer, that ends up leaving his career he loves so very m</span>
  <span id="freeText11221515897014080289" style="display:none"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1572489709ra/28378985.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>ABUSIVE THROUGHOUT...STAND-ALONE...3 DIFFERENT ENDINGS</b><br><br><b>
  <u>First Person Narrator: Sarah</u>
</b><br>The story right from the beginning starts with the ending. From there I was already aware that this would be an emotional book. I am glum right now because despite not liking the story, I connected with the characters. I also appreciate the author for her additional endings which has lifted my 1-star rating to a 2 making it slightly <i>OKAY</i>. <br><br>The father is a boxer, that ends up leaving his career he loves so very much after his wife became pregnant with their 2nd child wild she was still breastfeeding. Father had to work at a paper mill to support his family. <br><br>During this time, the father becomes bitter &amp; abuses his wife &amp; children physically. At 8 years old, James steps in front of his younger sister to protect her from their father's severe beating while taking the torture himself. This abusive behavior continues throughout the story. The father is a drunk, the mother is a drug addict that neglects to protect her children from the abuse of her husband. <br><br>The story then jumps to 11 years later. At 17, Sarah continues to be severely beaten by their father while James continues to defend her &amp; take their father's beatings though at this stage he holds his ground better. Sarah tries not to stay home alone with her father. She also fears he would one day rape her. This is a very dark book. <br><br>James &amp; Sarah plan on moving together after he saves enough to protect them both. As the story continues, James becomes overly protective &amp; a little delusional with Sarah. There gets to a point that James doesn't allow Sarah to plan any future that doesn't involve them being together. <br><br>James denies his sister any relationship with anyone other than himself. He continues to display obsession over her from trying to kiss her to control her. James' sister, Sarah, falls for his best friend Sam. Sam &amp; Sarah start dating behind his back for a few weeks. There is a camping trip with James, his sister, &amp; others. This is the only few times in the book that actually lights up a little. <br><br>Sam wants to tell James about his relationship with Sarah, but Sarah fears the worst will happen if James finds out. Sarah feels she is indebted to her brother for protecting her though she has mixed feelings with turning to Sam or staying with her brother for fear he'll lose it if she abandons him. The possessiveness is always strong from James' side. He is delusional, &amp; overbearing. <br><br>A lot of things happen into this story which never really drew me in. I could've finished this in 1 day, instead it took me 2 because I didn't want to read the story with all of the conflicting emotions. I had to finish because I needed to know what would happen after investing myself in it already. This has 3 endings. The first one the book ended with is the one that I will say is the original as the author left this in her book in Chapter 50. The other 2 were mainly to appease the readers I'm guessing as they are NOT part of any chapters in the book. If you want the alternate endings, then stop at Chapter 49. Chapter 50 is one, which wrecked me. Towards the end of the Kindle version e-book, the endings are after the acknowledgments all the way towards the end. <br><b>MY TAGS</b><br><u>DARK YA, TABOO, HEARTBREAKING, ABUSIVE PARENTS, CAGE FIGHT, BOXING (speaking through, not concentrated on this), HOMICIDE, SUICIDE, DRUGS, ATTEMPTED RAPE</u> <br><br>Click here if you want to know if this story has a HEA (Happily Ever After). <br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[The 3rd last ending is the HEA, the 2nd not so much, &amp; Chapter 50 is the worst, that one is a killer devastating gut-wrenching ending :( <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br>Stand-alone<br>Would I read it again? NO<br>Would I recommend it? NO (Depends how you like your stories, if you don't mind them dark, this one is for you!) <br>Are there Highlights to back up my review. A few. <br><br>READ THROUGH: KINDLE UNLIMITED<br><br>HOW MUCH IF THE SERIES WERE TO BE PURCHASED: $2.99 KINDLE EDITION<br><br>FREE READ WITH <b>KINDLE UNLIMITED</b> MEMBERSHIP FROM AMAZON / KINDLE<br><br>End of review. <br>Rambling<br><br>I started to read several reviews, &amp; for what I gathered this book is being compared to Forbidden. <b>DON'T</b>. It is different in its own way. It actually reminded me of this book until halfway though it's a German version translated &amp; was published on 2018 &amp; Flawed in 2012 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/42113870.Our_love_is_a_sin" title="Our love is a sin by Bettina Ellmann" rel="nofollow noopener">Our love is a sin</a> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/42113870.Our_love_is_a_sin" title="Our love is a sin by Bettina Ellmann" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/books/1538445978l/42113870._SY75_.jpg" alt="Our love is a sin by Bettina Ellmann" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a>.<br><br>Also this book you either love it or you hate it. In my case, I can't hate it because I did feel emotions with the characters. It just took a lot for me to get into because I couldn't with all of the constant abuse. It is a book that you think about though. I don't recommend it to those that like a cheerful book despite the ending. This one has 3.<br><br></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="11221515897014080289" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ZgtLSKqEuKXT29+5wCutGgUcWg/g/GjkiOkHm5XzabZAyOB1ebTXSGXE9HHxN0WlCCvTlSKC0fNsYkaQQHlLTA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }
